The passage mentions about a dozen issues that caused serious conflict. Think of a time when a small number of differences caused you to disparage another Muslim's beliefs. How does Maqrizi's account challenge you to reassess your reaction?

Maturidi's Precedence and the 40 Disputed Issues
Praise of Maturidi, enumeration of 40 disputed issues, and a call to study detailed sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Maturidi's pioneering role in defending Sunni creed, the enumeration of 40 key issues between Maturidis and Ash'aris, and the importance of studying detailed sources over later summaries.

Core Idea
Maturidi's full works and the 40 issues demand deep study, not shortcuts.

This lesson introduces a key moment in Maturidi history: Imam al-Maturidi's precedence in defending the creed, the enumeration of 40 differences with Ash'aris, and a call to study the proper sources. The passage also warns against lazily sticking to later summaries, reminding us that true understanding comes from engaging with the longer works.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify main points
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the sequence: praise of Maturidi, counting of 40 issues, recommendation of books, and critique of lazy students.
Notice the strong language used to criticize imitation.
2
Reflect on the significance of the 40 issues
Consider why the author emphasizes that Shaykhzada counted exactly 40 issues and argued against Ash'aris. This shows a systematic approach to differences.
3
Consider the methodological lesson
The author criticizes students who only study summaries. Ask yourself: why is it important to go beyond summaries to the longer works?
This connects to the broader Islamic pedagogical tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللإمام الماتريدي السَّبَقُ في حمل لواء الدفاع عن العقيدة الإسلامية ضد من خالفها من المبتدعة، وكتاب التوحيد للإمام خير شاهد على قوة علم الإمام، ودقة نظره، وعمق فكره، واتساع معارفه، إلا أن بعض الباحثين يستسهل الأمر، ويُقَلِّدُ مَنْ قبله دون وعي أو إدراك. وقد عد المسائل التي اختلف فيها الماتريدي والأشعري الإمام عبد الرحمن بن علي الشهير بشيخ زاده في كتابه نظم الفرائد وجمع الفوائد (۳) فأوصلها إلى أربعين مسألة، ناقش في جميع هذه المسائل الأشعرية ورَدَّ عليهم. وقد فصل كل هذه الأمور الإمام النسفي في كتابه الجليل القدر «تبصرة الأدلة» وهو من أفضل ما كُتب في علم الكلام على الإطلاق، ومثله كتاب أصول الدين للإمام الحجة فخر الإسلام البزدوي، ولكن ضعفُ هِمَمِ بعض الطلبة وتكاسلهم تدفعهم إلى التقليد والاقتصار على المتون المتأخرة، فلا يتعدونها إلى المطوَّلات والشروحات التي فيها العلم كله.
And Imam al-Maturidi has precedence in carrying the banner of defense of the Islamic creed against those who opposed it from among the innovators. And the book al-Tawhid of the Imam is the best witness to the strength of his knowledge, the precision of his vision, the depth of his thought, and the breadth of his knowledge. However, some researchers make the matter easy and imitate those before them without awareness or perception. And the issues in which al-Maturidi and al-Ash'ari differed were counted by Imam Abd al-Rahman ibn Ali known as Shaykhzada in his book Nazm al-Fara'id wa-Jam' al-Fawa'id, and he enumerated them as forty issues, and he discussed all these issues against the Ash'aris and refuted them. And Imam al-Nasafi detailed all these matters in his highly esteemed book Tabṣirat al-Adilla, which is among the best written in ilm al-kalam absolutely, and likewise the book Usul al-Din of Imam al-Hujja Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi. But the weakness of the determination of some students and their laziness pushes them to imitation and confinement to the later texts, not going beyond them to the longer works and commentaries which contain all knowledge.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage highlights Imam al-Maturidi's pioneering role in defending the Sunni creed. The author points to Maturidi's book 'al-Tawhid' as evidence of his scholarly excellence. He then criticizes later researchers who take the matter lightly and simply follow others without deep understanding. He mentions that Shaykhzada counted 40 issues of difference between the two schools in his work 'Nazm al-Fara'id wa-Jam' al-Fawa'id', where he argued against the Ash'ari positions. The author then recommends two key works that thoroughly discuss these issues: Imam al-Nasafi's 'Tabṣirat al-Adilla' and Imam al-Bazdawi's 'Usul al-Din'. He laments that many students, due to laziness, restrict themselves to studying only the later short texts (mutūn muta'akhkhira) and avoid the longer works that contain the full science. This is a methodological criticism: true understanding requires engaging with the detailed sources, not just summaries.

Key Disputed Issues between Maturidis and Ash'aris
Enumeration of six disputed issues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand six key theological issues over which the Maturidi and Ash'ari schools diverge.

Core Idea
These six issues define the main doctrinal fault lines between Maturidis and Ash'aris.

The author presents a concise list of central points of disagreement between the two major Sunni theological schools. While not exhaustive, these issues—ranging from the role of intellect to the nature of divine attributes—capture the most significant doctrinal differences. Let's examine each one briefly.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note that this is a simple enumeration.
2
Identify each issue
List the six issues mentioned. For each, consider what theological area it concerns (e.g., intellect, attributes, human capacity).
3
Connect to broader debates
Think about why each issue matters. For example, the issue of 'intellect' relates to how humans know God.
4
Recognize the modesty of the list
The author says 'and other issues'—this is just a sample. Understand that there are many more points of difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن مسائل الخلاف بين الماتريدية والأشعرية مسألة العقل، ومسألة التكوين والمكوّن، ومسألة القوة على الطاعة وعلى المعصية، ومسألة حدوث صفات الأفعال، ومسألة تعلق صفة السمع والبصر بالمسموعات والمبصرات، ومسألة تكليف ما لا يُطاق (١)، وغيرها من المسائل التي يطول ذكرها.
And among the issues of dispute between the Maturidis and Ash'aris are: the issue of the intellect, the issue of takwin and the thing brought into being (mukawwan), the issue of the capacity for obedience and capacity for disobedience, the issue of the origination of the attributes of actions, the issue of the attachment of the attribute of hearing and seeing to the things heard and seen, and the issue of taxing (taklif) what cannot be borne, and other issues whose mention would be lengthy.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage enumerates six key theological issues over which the Maturidi and Ash'ari schools differ: 1) The role and nature of the intellect (al-ʿaql); 2) The relationship between God's creative action (takwīn) and the created thing (mukawwan); 3) The human capacity (quwwa) for obedience and for sin; 4) Whether the attributes of actions (ṣifāt al-afʿāl) are eternal or originated; 5) The manner in which the divine attributes of hearing and seeing relate to their objects (whether they are independent of the objects); and 6) The possibility of imposing a duty that cannot be fulfilled (taklif ma la yutaq). The author notes that there are many other issues beyond these.

تكليف ما لا يُطاق

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Does this dispute challenge you to prioritize divine guidance over your own logic? What would change if you truly submitted your mind to the Quran and Sunnah?
?
Reflect on the issue of 'taxing what cannot be borne' (taklīf mā lā yuṭāq). Have you ever felt that a command from God or life's trials were beyond your strength? How does the Maturidi-Ash'ari debate on this matter influence your perspective on God's mercy and your own accountability? Will you trust that Allah never burdens a soul beyond its capacity, even when you feel overwhelmed?
?
Consider that these six disputes represent real theological fault lines that scholars debated. But beyond intellectual knowledge, ask yourself: does knowing about these differences bring you closer to understanding the greatness of Allah and His attributes, or do they become mere academic curiosities? Resolve to learn the position of Ahl al-Sunnah on each issue with humility, seeking to strengthen your faith, not just your knowledge.

Major Disputes Between Maturidis and Ash'aris
Nasafi lists key theological disagreements between Maturidis and Ash'aris.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key theological issues that divide Maturidis and Ash'aris as enumerated by Imam Nasafi.

Core Idea
Nasafi lists six foundational disagreements separating two Sunni schools.

This lesson presents a direct enumeration from Imam Nasafi's Bahr al-Kalam of the major theological disputes between the Maturidi and Ash'ari schools. By memorizing this list, you gain a map of Sunni intra-school differences. The passage names six specific issues, along with a reference to many more.

Guided Path
1

The footnote marker (١) indicates a longer discussion follows in the original text.
2
Identify each issue
Go through the list and for each issue, note the Arabic term and its English equivalent. These are the key topics of debate.
The issues are: al-'aql, takwin/mukawwan, quwwa, huduth sifat al-af'al, sam'/basar, taklif ma la yutaq.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن مسائل الخلاف بين الماتريدية والأشعرية مسألة العقل، ومسألة التكوين والمكوّن، ومسألة القوة على الطاعة وعلى المعصية، ومسألة حدوث صفات الأفعال، ومسألة تعلق صفة السمع والبصر بالمسموعات والمبصرات، ومسألة تكليف ما لا يُطاق (١)، وغيرها من المسائل التي يطول ذكرها.

Commentary

The footnote marker at number six indicates a longer discussion follows. He then indicates there are many more issues beyond these. This list gives a snapshot of major theological fault lines.

Views on Createdness of Divine Definition and Human Knowledge
Nasafi presents three positions on createdness of definition and knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differing positions of Mu'tazila, Mafrugiyya, and Ahl al-Sunna on the createdness of divine definition and human knowledge.

Core Idea
God's defining is uncreated; human knowledge is created.

This lesson presents three theological schools' views on whether the divine act of defining (ta'rif) and human knowledge (ma'rifa) are created or uncreated. The Mu'tazila and philosophers say both are created. Another group, the Mafrugiyya, says both are uncreated. The Sunni position distinguishes between the two, resolving the dilemma.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through.
2
Identify the three positions
List each group mentioned and what they claim about definition and knowledge. Notice the key terms 'مخلوق' and 'غير مخلوق'.
The groups are: Mu'tazila & Mutafalsifa, Mafrugiyya, and Ahl al-Sunna.
3
Focus on the Sunni distinction
Ahl al-Sunna do not say both are created or both are uncreated. They distinguish between God's definition (uncreated) and human knowledge (created). Why might this be important?
This avoids making God's attribute created or elevating human knowledge to divine status.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this distinction preserves God's transcendence while acknowledging the reality of human knowledge. How does it affect faith and disbelief?
This ties into broader debates about the createdness of the Qur'an.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالت المعتزلة والمتقشفة: كلاهما مخلوقان، وهو التعريف والمعرفة، وقالت المفروغية: كلاهما غير مخلوقين، وهو التعريف والمعرفة.
وعند أهل السنة والجماعة التعريف من الله تعالى غير مخلوق، والمعرفة والتعريف من العبد مخلوق.
And the Mu'tazila and the Mutafalsifa said: Both are created, i.e., the definition and knowledge. And the Mafrugiyya said: Both are uncreated, i.e., the definition and knowledge.
And according to Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, the definition from God Most High is uncreated, and the knowledge from the servant is created.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a classification of theological positions on whether the divine 'definition' (ta'rif) and human 'knowledge' (ma'rifa) are created or uncreated. The Mu'tazila and the 'Mutafalsifa' (perhaps a variant of 'philosophers' or a sect) claim both are created. Another group, the 'Mafrugiyya' (possibly a branch of the Murji'a?), claim both are uncreated. The Sunni position distinguishes: God's act of defining is uncreated (as it is an attribute of God), but the knowledge that results in the servant is created. This resolves the dilemma by avoiding both extremes: it neither makes God's attribute created nor elevates human knowledge to the divine level.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
المتقشفة
المفروغية
أهل السنة والجماعة
مخلوق
غير مخلوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the Sunni position aligns with either the Mu'tazila or the Mafrugiyya.
Correction: The Sunni position uniquely distinguishes between God's defining (uncreated) and human knowledge (created).

Checkpoint

A) The knowledge in the servant's heart
B) The definition from God
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position distinguishes between God's uncreated definition and created human knowledge, avoiding both extremes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat your own knowledge of God as if it were absolute and uncreated, or do you humbly acknowledge that it is created, limited, and subject to error? What daily habit reflects your answer?
?
When you hear or read interpretations of God's attributes, do you mentally distinguish between the uncreated truth of God's definition and the created human attempt to understand it? How can you make this distinction a guard against arrogance?
?
Your knowledge of the Deen is created—it did not exist before you learned it. Does this truth move you to gratitude toward the One who gave it, or does it expose a hidden pride in what you 'know'? What will you do today to keep this awareness alive?

Sectarian Views on Ta'rif and Ma'rifa
Nasafi states the positions of Mu'tazila, Mutashabbiha, Mufarrughiyya, and Ahl al-Sunna on ta'rif and ma'rifa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differing positions of early Islamic sects on whether the act of defining (ta'rif) and the resulting knowledge (ma'rifa) are created or uncreated, and the Sunni middle position.

Core Idea
The Sunni position distinguishes divine ta'rif (uncreated) from human ta'rif and ma'rifa (created).

This passage from Imam Nasafi introduces a key debate in kalam: are the processes of defining and knowing created or eternal? Various sects took extreme positions, either declaring both created or both uncreated. Nasafi presents the Sunni resolution that carefully distinguishes between what belongs to Allah and what belongs to the servant.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the groups
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Identify the three groups mentioned: Mu'tazila/Mutashabbiha, Mufarrughiyya, and Ahl al-Sunna. Note what each group claims about ta'rif and ma'rifa.
2
Understand the Sunni distinction
Focus on the Sunni position: al-ta'rif from Allah is uncreated, but al-ma'rifa and al-ta'rif from the servant are created. This distinction preserves Allah's eternal speech while acknowledging human temporality.
The key is the source of the act: divine vs. human.
3
Reflect on the theological significance
Ask yourself: why does this matter? If all knowledge were uncreated, it would blur the line between Creator and creation. If all were created, it would deny Allah's eternal attribute of speech. The Sunni middle path upholds both tawhid and human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالت المعتزلة والمتقشفة: كلاهما مخلوقان، وهو التعريف والمعرفة، وقالت المفروغية: كلاهما غير مخلوقين، وهو التعريف والمعرفة. وعند أهل السنة والجماعة التعريف من الله تعالى غير مخلوق، والمعرفة والتعريف من العبد مخلوق.
And the Mu'tazila and the Mutashabbiha said: Both are created, meaning al-ta'rif (definition) and al-ma'rifa (knowledge). And the Mufarrughiyya said: Both are uncreated, meaning al-ta'rif and al-ma'rifa. And according to Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, al-ta'rif from Allah is uncreated, and al-ma'rifa and al-ta'rif from the servant are created.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage defines the doctrinal positions on whether the act of defining (ta'rif) and the resulting knowledge (ma'rifa) are created or uncreated. The Mu'tazila and Mutashabbiha hold that both are created. The Mufarrughiyya sect holds that both are uncreated. Ahl al-Sunna takes a middle position: the ta'rif that comes from Allah is uncreated (i.e., His speech or definition), but the ma'rifa and ta'rif that occur within the servant are created (i.e., human acts of knowing and defining). This distinction preserves Allah's eternal attribute of speech while acknowledging the temporality of human acquisition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Ahl al-Sunna considers all knowledge or definitions uncreated, because they affirm the uncreatedness of the Qur'an.
Correction: The passage clarifies that only al-ta'rif from Allah is uncreated; the ma'rifa and ta'rif that occur within the servant are created. This avoids equating human acts with divine attributes.

Checkpoint

B) Al-ta'rif from Allah
C) Both al-ta'rif and al-ma'rifa
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position safeguards Allah's eternal attribute of speech while affirming the temporality of human acts of knowing and defining.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Reflect on a time you were absolutely certain of your religious opinion. Did you consider whether that certainty came from Allah's uncreated truth or your own created reasoning? What change does that question demand from you today?
?
If human ma'rifa is created and therefore fallible, are you willing to hold your interpretations of the Qur'an and Sunnah with humility, open to correction? What is one specific belief you have about Islam that you need to re-examine with this in mind?

The Mushabbiha's Proof Texts and the Salaf's Response
Lists verses and hadith used by anthropomorphists and gives the Salaf's methodological response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Salaf responded to anthropomorphic interpretations of ambiguous Quranic verses and hadith by affirming the texts without speculating about their modality.

Core Idea
Affirm the revealed attributes, but do not ask 'how'.

This passage tackles a key theological dispute: the Mushabbiha (anthropomorphists) take certain verses and hadith literally, implying bodily attributes for Allah. In response, the early Salaf, exemplified by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, established a principled methodology: affirm the truth of the revelation, but refrain from investigating the modality (kayfiyya). This lesson will unpack both the proofs used by the Mushabbiha and the decisive Salafi principle that safeguards divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once, then the translation. Notice how the passage first presents the Mushabbiha's evidence and then gives the Salaf's response.
Pay attention to the examples of verses and hadith cited.
2
Identify the two main sections
The passage has two clear parts: the Mushabbiha's use of apparent meanings (zahir) of texts, and the response by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. Locate the boundary.
3
Analyze the Salafi principle
Understand the phrase 'nؤminu bima ja'a min 'indi Allah wa la nashtaghilu bi kayfiyyatih' – we believe without occupying ourselves with how. This is the core of the lesson.
This is a classic tafwid (consignment of meaning) but with affirmation of the text.
4
Reflect on the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding: some think this response rejects the attributes entirely. But the Salaf affirm the attributes while negating modality.
This is not tafwid of the attribute itself, but tafwid of its modality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالحاصل أن المشبهة يتمسكون بظاهر الآيات نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ هَالِكُ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُ ﴾ [العنكبوت: ۸۸] وقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الْجَلَالِ وَالْإِكْرَامِ ﴾ [الرحمن: ٢٧]. وبالأخبار المتشابهات نحو قوله : ( إن الله تعالى خلق آدم بيده، وكتب التوراة بیده، وخلق جنة عدن بيده وغرس شجرة طوبى بيده» (۱). وفي رواية: «أنه خلق الإبل بيده [ وخلق جنة عدن بيده ](۲)) . وعن محمد بن الحسن رحمه الله إنا نقول : نؤمن بما جاء من عند الله تعالى، ولا نشتغل بكيفيته، على ما أراد (۳) الله تعالى، وبما جاء من عند رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم على ما أراد به رسول الله . [ وهو إخبار كثير من كبراء الأئمة وعلماء أهل الملة ] (٤).
The conclusion is that the anthropomorphists (mushabbiha) cling to the apparent meanings of verses, such as His saying: 'Everything is perishing except His Face' [al-Ankabut: 88] and His saying: 'And there remains the Face of your Lord, Possessor of Majesty and Honor' [al-Rahman: 27]. And from the ambiguous hadith such as his saying: 'Indeed Allah created Adam with His hand, and wrote the Torah with His hand, and created the Garden of Eden with His hand, and planted the tree of Tuba with His hand.' (1) And in a narration: 'He created the camels with His hand [and created the Garden of Eden with His hand]' (2). And from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, may Allah have mercy on him: 'We say: We believe in what has come from Allah Almighty, and we do not occupy ourselves with its modality, according to what Allah intended (3), and in what has come from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, according to what the Messenger of Allah intended by it.' [And this is the report of many of the senior imams and scholars of the people of the religion.] (4).
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the anthropomorphist (mushabbiha) methodology and a presentation of the correct Salafi approach. It begins by stating that the anthropomorphists hold onto the apparent (ظاهر) meanings of certain verses and hadith, citing examples: the verses 'كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه' (Everything perishes except His Face) and 'ويبقى وجه ربك' (And there remains the Face of your Lord) which they take to imply a literal 'face' and thus a body. Also hadith that mention Allah's 'hand' in creating Adam, the Torah, the Garden, etc. The passage then presents the response of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan (likely a Hanafi scholar): the correct position is to believe in what has come from Allah and His messenger without delving into 'how' (كيفية). This is a classic principle of the Salaf regarding ambiguous texts (mutashabihat): affirm the truth of the revelation, but refrain from speculating about the modality, leaving the true meaning to Allah and His messenger. The final comment notes that this is the position of many senior imams.

Key Terms
المشبهة
ظاهر الآيات
الأخبار المتشابهات
اليد
الوجه
الكيفية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Salaf's response is a form of tafwid (consigning the meaning to Allah) without affirmation of the attribute itself.
Correction: The Salaf affirm the attributes (like Hand, Face) as real attributes of Allah, but they negate knowledge of their modality (kayfiyya). They do not deny the attribute, nor do they interpret it metaphorically.

Checkpoint

A) To interpret them literally
B) To reject them as false
C) To believe in them without asking how
D) To speculate about their meaning

Key Takeaway
The Salaf respond to anthropomorphic proof texts by affirming the divine attributes mentioned while completely refraining from speculating about their modality.

The Mushabbihah's Literalism and the Sound Response of Tafwid
Nasafi describes the Mushabbihah's literalism and presents tafwid as the correct response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mushabbihah's approach of literalism leads to anthropomorphism and how the early scholars responded by affirming the texts while negating modality (tafwid).

Core Idea
Affirm the texts, but do not ask 'how' — tafwid protects tawhid.

In this passage, Nasafi identifies a key theological error: the Mushabbihah (anthropomorphists) cling to the literal wording of Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths, interpreting them in a way that implies a physical deity. He then presents the balanced approach of the early Sunni imams, transmitted from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, which is to affirm what has come from Allah and His Messenger without delving into the modality. This lesson unpacks that methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
Read the passage and notice how Nasafi contrasts the Mushabbihah, who cling to literal texts, with the orthodox response that follows.
The Mushabbihah are named from 'tashbih' (assimilation), meaning they liken Allah to creation.
2
Examine the cited texts
Look at the verses and hadiths mentioned. What do they have in common? They all use terms like 'face' and 'hand' that could be misinterpreted.
These are verses of attributes that require careful handling.
3
Focus on the orthodox response
Read the statement of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. What is the key phrase that defines the correct approach? 'We do not occupy ourselves with its modality.'
This is the essence of tafwid: consigning the true meaning to Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالحاصل أن المشبهة يتمسكون بظاهر الآيات نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ هَالِكُ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُ ﴾ [العنكبوت: ۸۸] وقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الْجَلَالِ وَالْإِكْرَامِ ﴾ [الرحمن: ٢٧]. وبالأخبار المتشابهات نحو قوله : ( إن الله تعالى خلق آدم بيده، وكتب التوراة بیده، وخلق جنة عدن بيده وغرس شجرة طوبى بيده). وفي رواية: «أنه خلق الإبل بيده [ وخلق جنة عدن بيده ]). وعن محمد بن الحسن رحمه الله إنا نقول : نؤمن بما جاء من عند الله تعالى، ولا نشتغل بكيفيته، على ما أراد الله تعالى، وبما جاء من عند رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم على ما أراد به رسول الله . [ وهو إخبار كثير من كبراء الأئمة وعلماء أهل الملة ].
The conclusion is that the Mushabbihah cling to the apparent meanings of verses, such as His statement: 'Everything is perishing except His Face' [al-Ankabut: 88], and His statement: 'And the Face of your Lord, full of Majesty and Honor, will remain forever' [al-Rahman: 27]. And with ambiguous hadiths, such as his statement: 'Indeed Allah created Adam with His hand, wrote the Torah with His hand, created the Garden of Eden with His hand, and planted the tree of Tuba with His hand.' And in a narration: 'He created the camel with His hand [and created the Garden of Eden with His hand].' And from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan (may Allah have mercy on him): We say: We believe in what came from Allah, and we do not occupy ourselves with its modality, according to what Allah intended, and in what came from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) according to what the Messenger intended. And this is a report from many of the senior imams and scholars of the people of the faith.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage identifies a theological problem and provides the orthodox response. It begins by describing the Mushabbihah (anthropomorphists), who cling to the literal text of certain Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths. The verses cited are those that mention the 'Face' of Allah, and the hadiths mention Allah's 'hand' in creating Adam, writing the Torah, and creating Paradise. The author then transmits the stance of the Hanafi jurist Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, who states the correct methodology: affirm what has come from Allah and His Messenger without investigating the modality (kayfiyyah). This is the approach of tafwid (consigning the true meaning to Allah). The passage concludes by noting that this position is reported from many senior imams and scholars, thus giving it authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that believing in the literal meaning of these texts without interpretation is the same as corporealism.
Correction: The early scholars affirmed the texts while negating any likeness to creation; they did not interpret them in a corporeal sense.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The orthodox response to ambiguous attributes is tafwid: affirming the text while negating modality and avoiding both ta'til (negation) and tashbih (assimilation).

The Real Dispute: Kalam Nafsi vs. Kalam Lafzi
Clarifies that the real difference is over kalam nafsi and proves it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the real disagreement between Ahl al-Sunnah and the Hanabila over the Quran is about affirming or negating inner speech (kalam nafsi) rather than the verbal expression being created or uncreated.

Core Idea
The Quran debate is not about words but about Allah's eternal attribute of speech.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi cuts through the confusion surrounding the createdness of the Quran. He explains that the Hanabila mistakenly equated 'uncreated' with 'non-accidental,' but the core issue is whether Allah has an eternal inner speech. This lesson clarifies that Ahl al-Sunnah affirm eternal inner speech while agreeing that the composed words are temporal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how Imam Nasafi first critiques the Hanabila, then states the real point of contention, provides a proof, and finally rebuts the opponents' arguments.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two positions
What do the Hanabila claim? What do Ahl al-Sunnah affirm? The author says the Hanabila placed 'uncreated' in the position of 'non-accidental', but the real dispute is about affirming or negating inner speech.
Ahl al-Sunnah do not claim words are eternal.
3
Grasp the proof for inner speech
The proof: Allah is described as 'speaker' by consensus; temporal speech cannot subsist in His essence; therefore His speech must be eternal inner speech.
This is the key argument.
4
Understand the rebuttal
The opponents argue that the Quran is composed, revealed, Arabic, etc. But these are marks of temporal things. The author says this only refutes those who claim the very letters are eternal, not us (Ahl al-Sunnah).
We affirm the meaning is eternal, the expression is created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذهب إليه الحنابلة جهلاً أو عنادًا، وأقام غير مخلوق مقام غير حادث تنبيها على اتحادهما وقصدًا إلى جري الكلام على وفق الحديث، حيث قال : القرءان كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق، ومن قال إنه مخلوق فهو كافر بالله العظيم، وتنصيصا على محل الخلاف بالعبارة المشهورة فيما بين الفرقتين وهو أن القرءان مخلوق أو غير مخلوق، ولهذا تترجم ا المسألة بمسألة خلق القرءان، وتحقيق الخلاف بيننا وبينهم يرجع إلى إثبات الكلام النفسي ونفيه، وإلا فنحن لا نقول بقدم الألفاظ والحروف وهم لا يقولون بحدوث الكلام النفسي. ودليلنا ما مر أنه ثبت بالإجماع وتواتر النقل عن الأنبياء صلوات الله عليهم أنه تعالى متكلم، ولا معنى له سوى أنه متصف بالكلام، ويمتنع قيام اللفظي الحادث بذاته تعالى، فتعيَّن النفسي القديم، وأما استدلالهم بأن القرءان متصف بما هو من صفات المخلوقين وسمات الحدوث من التأليف والتنظيم والإنزال والتنزيل وكونه عربيًا مسموعا فصيحا معجزًا إلى غير ذلك، فإنما يقوم حجة على الحنابلة لا علينا، لأنا قائلون بحدوث النظم، وإنما الكلام في المعنى القديم.
The Hanabila adopted that out of ignorance or stubbornness, and they placed 'uncreated' in the position of 'non-accidental' as a hint at their union and intending to make the statement run according to the hadith where he said: 'The Quran is the speech of Allah, uncreated, and whoever says it is created is a disbeliever in Allah the Great.' And specifying the point of disagreement with the famous phrase between the two sects—that the Quran is created or uncreated. For this reason, the issue is named the issue of the creation of the Quran. The reality of the disagreement between us and them reduces to affirming inner speech (al-kalam al-nafsi) or negating it. Otherwise, we do not say the words and letters are eternal, and they do not say that inner speech is temporal. Our proof is what has passed: it is established by consensus and frequent transmission from the prophets (peace be upon them) that He the Exalted is a speaker (mutakallim), and there is no meaning to that except that He is described by speech. It is impossible for temporal verbal speech to subsist in His essence, so the eternal inner speech is determined. As for their argument that the Quran is characterized by attributes of created beings and marks of temporality—composition, organization, revelation, sending down, being Arabic, audible, eloquent, miraculous, etc.—that is only a proof against the Hanabila, not against us, for we affirm the temporality of composition, and the speech is about the eternal meaning.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage clarifies the real nature of the dispute between Ahl al-Sunnah and the Hanabila (a reference to certain literalist groups) on the issue of the Quran's createdness. The author explains that Hanabila misguidedly equated 'uncreated' with 'non-accidental', but the real point is about kalam nafsi (inner, eternal speech) versus lafzi (verbal, temporal speech). Ahl al-Sunnah affirm that Allah is mutakallim (speaker) by virtue of eternal speech subsisting in His essence, not by temporal letters and sounds. The proof given: consensus and transmission establish that Allah is a speaker; temporal speech cannot subsist in His essence, so eternal inner speech must be affirmed. The opponents' arguments about the Quran's composed, revealed, Arabic nature are valid only against those who say the very letters are eternal—not against those who say the meaning is eternal and the expression is created. Thus the dispute is truly about kalam nafsi, not about the verbal expression.

غير مخلوق

الكلام اللفظي
القديم
الحادث
النظم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the dispute is only about whether the physical Quran is created or uncreated, ignoring the deeper issue of Allah's attribute of speech.
Correction: The passage shows that the real disagreement is about affirming or negating inner speech (kalam nafsi) as an eternal attribute of Allah, not about the createdness of the verbal expression.

Checkpoint

A) Whether the Quran is Arabic or not.
B) Whether the Quran is memorized or written.
C) Whether Allah speaks with inner eternal speech (kalam nafsi) or not.
D) Whether the Quran was revealed in one night or gradually.

Key Takeaway
The dispute over the Quran's createdness ultimately hinges on whether Allah has an eternal attribute of inner speech (kalam nafsi).

Claims that the Quran is Created
Opponents' claims that the Quran is created

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the arguments made by deviant sects to claim that the Quran is created.

Core Idea
Deviant sects claimed the Quran is created, citing its temporal speech and the absurdity of commanding non-existence.

Before we examine the Sunni position, we must first understand what the opponents say. This passage presents the views of al-Najariyya, al-Mutashabbiha, al-Mu'tazila, and al-Jahmiyya, who argued that the Quran is created and temporal. They offered specific reasons for their claim, including that Allah spoke it only on the Night of Power and that it would be unwise to command non-existent beings.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponents' claims
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the groups mentioned and their core assertion that the Quran is created and temporal.
The footnote markers (١) and (٢) refer to textual notes; focus on the arguments themselves.
2
Identify the specific arguments
Find the two arguments the opponents give: (1) the Quran was spoken on the Night of Power, not before; (2) the Quran contains commands and prohibitions, and commanding non-existent beings is unwise.
These arguments are meant to support their claim of createdness.
3
Reflect on the logic
Consider why the opponents think commanding non-existent beings is unwise. This is a key point that the Sunni proof will address.
The issue of commanding the non-existent is a known theological debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال النجارية، والمتقشفة (١) ، والمعتزلة والجهمية لعنهم الله (٢): القرآن محدث ومخلوق. وقالوا: القرآن تكلّم به ليلة القدر، ولم يتكلم قبل ذلك. وقالوا: القرآن أوامر ونواه، وليس من الحكمة أن يأمر المعدوم. وحجة أهل السنة والجماعة في أن كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق، لأنه لو كان مخلوقا لا يخلو إما أن خَلَقَه في غير ذاته أو في ذاته، فإن كان مخلوقا في غير ذاته لكان المتكلم ذلك الذات، لأن المتكلم من قام به صفة الكلام، كالأسود والأحمر اسم لشخص قام
And al-Najariyya, al-Mutashabbiha [؟], and al-Mu'tazila and al-Jahmiyya (may Allah curse them) said: The Quran is temporal and created. And they said: The Quran was spoken on the Night of Power, and He had not spoken before that. And they said: The Quran contains commands and prohibitions, and it is not wise to command that which does not exist. And the proof of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah that the speech of Allah the Exalted is uncreated is: if it were created, then either He created it in other than His essence or in His essence. If it is created in other than His essence, then that essence would be the speaker, because the speaker is the one in whom the attribute of speech subsists, just as 'black' and 'red' are names for a person in whom [those attributes] subsist.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage first states the positions of various deviant groups: al-Najariyya, al-Mutashabbiha (or al-Mutafalsifa as per footnote), al-Mu'tazila, and al-Jahmiyya. They claim the Quran is temporal and created, that Allah spoke it only on the Night of Power (not before), and that commanding non-existent beings is unwise. Then the author presents the proof of Ahl al-Sunnah: If the Quran were created, it must have been created either outside Allah's essence or within it. If created outside, then that external locus would be the speaker—absurd, because the speaker is the one in whom speech subsists. If created inside His essence, then His essence would be a locus for temporal events, which is impossible. The argument is cut off but clearly demonstrates the impossibility of the Quran being created. The analogy of 'black' and 'red' indicates that attributes subsist in the subject; similarly, speech must subsist in the speaker, and if created elsewhere, that other being would be the speaker.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the opponents' argument about commanding non-existent is logically sound and that the Quran must therefore be created.
Correction: The Sunni position refutes this by showing that Allah's knowledge and speech are eternal; commanding non-existent beings is not unwise because Allah knows they will exist in the future.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the groups mentioned as claiming the Quran is created?
A) al-Najariyya
B) al-Mutashabbiha
C) al-Qadariyya
D) al-Jahmiyya

Key Takeaway
Deviant sects argued the Quran is created based on its temporal speech and the perceived irrationality of commanding non-existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the claim that commanding non-existent beings is irrational, do you feel a tug in your heart to agree? Have you ever judged a divine command based on whether it seemed wise to your limited mind? What does this passage teach you about the danger of measuring Allah's actions by human standards? Commit today to submit to every command of the Quran, even when your intellect questions it.
?
The deviant sects argued that the Quran must be created because it was spoken on Laylat al-Qadr. Do you ever unconsciously reduce the Quran to a book that 'started' at a point in history, forgetting that the speech of Allah is eternal? How can you train your heart to revere the Quran as uncreated, beginningless speech? What will you change about your relationship with the Quran this week to reflect that belief?
?
The author curses these sects for their error. Do you take the doctrine of the uncreated Quran seriously enough to reject even seemingly plausible arguments that contradict it? Are there any areas of your 'aql (intellect) where you have allowed reasoning to override revelation? Ask Allah to protect you from such deviation and to root your faith in submission, not speculation.

The Sunni Proof Against the Quran's Createdness
Sunni proof using disjunction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first part of the Sunni rational proof that the Quran cannot be created, based on the disjunction of creation inside or outside Allah's essence.

Core Idea
If the Quran were created, it must be either inside or outside Allah's essence — both lead to absurdity.

After presenting the opponents' view, Imam al-Nasafi now begins the Sunni refutation. The proof is based on a simple logical disjunction: if the Quran were created, where would that creation occur? The first scenario — creation outside of Allah — leads to an obvious absurdity, as the external locus would then have to be the speaker, not Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Focus on the logical structure: a disjunction (either inside or outside) and the first case.
The passage cuts off, but we have the first branch fully presented.
2
Understand the disjunction
The proof begins with a dichotomy: if the Quran were created, it must be created either within Allah's essence or outside it. These are the only possibilities.
This is a classic rational argument form.
3
Analyze the first case
If the Quran were created outside Allah's essence, then that external thing (e.g., a tablet or heavens) would be the speaker, because speech is an attribute that subsists in a subject. The analogy with 'black' and 'red' clarifies this.
The analogy: just as 'black' names a person in whom blackness subsists, 'speaker' names the one in whom speech subsists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال النجارية، والمتقشفة (١) ، والمعتزلة والجهمية لعنهم الله (٢): القرآن محدث ومخلوق. وقالوا: القرآن تكلّم به ليلة القدر، ولم يتكلم قبل ذلك. وقالوا: القرآن أوامر ونواه، وليس من الحكمة أن يأمر المعدوم. وحجة أهل السنة والجماعة في أن كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق، لأنه لو كان مخلوقا لا يخلو إما أن خَلَقَه في غير ذاته أو في ذاته، فإن كان مخلوقا في غير ذاته لكان المتكلم ذلك الذات، لأن المتكلم من قام به صفة الكلام، كالأسود والأحمر اسم لشخص قام
And al-Najariyya, al-Mutashabbiha [؟], and al-Mu'tazila and al-Jahmiyya (may Allah curse them) said: The Quran is temporal and created. And they said: The Quran was spoken on the Night of Power, and He had not spoken before that. And they said: The Quran contains commands and prohibitions, and it is not wise to command that which does not exist. And the proof of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah that the speech of Allah the Exalted is uncreated is: if it were created, then either He created it in other than His essence or in His essence. If it is created in other than His essence, then that essence would be the speaker, because the speaker is the one in whom the attribute of speech subsists, just as 'black' and 'red' are names for a person in whom [those attributes] subsist.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage first states the positions of various deviant groups: al-Najariyya, al-Mutashabbiha (or al-Mutafalsifa as per footnote), al-Mu'tazila, and al-Jahmiyya. They claim the Quran is temporal and created, that Allah spoke it only on the Night of Power (not before), and that commanding non-existent beings is unwise. Then the author presents the proof of Ahl al-Sunnah: If the Quran were created, it must have been created either outside Allah's essence or within it. If created outside, then that external locus would be the speaker—absurd, because the speaker is the one in whom speech subsists. If created inside His essence, then His essence would be a locus for temporal events, which is impossible. The argument is cut off but clearly demonstrates the impossibility of the Quran being created. The analogy of 'black' and 'red' indicates that attributes subsist in the subject; similarly, speech must subsist in the speaker, and if created elsewhere, that other being would be the speaker.

Key Terms
أهل السنة والجماعة
مخلوق
ذات
المتكلم
صفة الكلام
أسود
أحمر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the Quran being created does not affect who the speaker is; they might think Allah could create speech outside Himself and still be called the speaker.
Correction: The rational proof shows that speech is an attribute of the one in whom it subsists; if created outside, that external entity, not Allah, would be the speaker. This is a clear absurdity.

Checkpoint
According to the Sunni proof, if the Quran were created outside of Allah's essence, who would be the speaker?
A) Allah
B) The external locus (e.g., the tablet)
C) The angel Jibril
D) The Prophet Muhammad

Key Takeaway
The Sunni proof begins by showing that if the Quran were created outside Allah, then that external thing would have to be the speaker — an absurd conclusion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah, subsisting in His essence, then it is not like any other book. Commit today to read one ayah with full presence of heart, as if hearing it for the first time.
?
The proof shows that if the Quran were created outside Allah, another thing would have to be the speaker. But you know that Allah is the speaker. Yet do your actions show that you treat the Quran as authoritative? Which command from the Quran are you avoiding? Write it down, and make a specific plan to start obeying it this week.
?
Allah's speech is eternal. Your time is limited. You will be asked about what you did with His word. If you were to die today, would you be satisfied with your relationship with the Quran? What is one concrete step you will take after this lesson to increase your engagement with the Quran, not just as a ritual but as the living word of your Creator?

Inner Affirmation Is the Heart of Faith
Nasafi refutes the Karramiyya using Quran and hadith that tasdiq is a condition of iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why inner affirmation (tasdiq) is a necessary condition for iman, as proven by Quran and hadith against the Karramiyya.

Core Idea
Inner affirmation is the heart of faith, not just words.

The Karramiyya sect claimed that merely saying the shahada makes one a believer, even without inner conviction. Imam Nasafi refutes this using two clear proofs from the Qur'an and the Prophet's own words. This passage establishes that genuine faith requires inner sincerity and affirmation, not just outward utterance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without over-analyzing, then read the translation. Let the flow of the argument sink in.
Pay attention to the two proofs: a verse and a hadith.
2
Understand the Karramiyya position
The Karramiyya believed that mere verbal confession (qawl bi-l-lisan) constitutes iman, even without inner conviction. This makes their view vulnerable to the hypocrites' case.
The verse about hypocrites is specifically chosen to disprove them.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
Allah says that some people say 'We believe' but are not believers. This shows that verbal utterance alone is insufficient; inner affirmation must be present.
Nasafi concludes directly: 'So it is established that tasdiq is a condition for the soundness of iman.'
4
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever says, 'There is no god but Allah,' sincerely and with purity, enters paradise.' Sincerity (ikhlas) implies inner affirmation, not just words.
The hadith makes tasdiq a condition for entry into paradise.
5
Connect the two proofs
Both proofs converge: the verse denies iman to those who merely claim it verbally, and the hadith demands inner purity. Together they refute the Karramiyya.
This shows that iman requires both tongue and heart.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحجتنا على الكرامية قوله تعالى: { وَمِنَ النَّاسِ مَن يَقُولُ آمَنَّا بِاللَّهِ وَبِالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ وَمَا هُم بِمُؤْمِنِينَ } [البقرة: 8] فثبت أن التصديق شرط صحة الإيمان، ويدل عليه قوله عليه السلام: من قال لا إله إلا الله خالصًا مخلصًا دخل الجنة، شرط التصديق.
And our proof against the Karramiyya is His statement, the Exalted: 'And among the people are those who say, 'We have believed in Allah and the Last Day,' but they are not believers' (al-Baqarah 2:8). So it is established that tasdiq (affirmation) is a condition of the soundness of iman. And it is indicated by his statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever says: There is no god but Allah, sincerely and with purity, enters paradise' — he made tasdiq a condition.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This is a refutation of the Karramiyya sect, who held that iman consists of mere verbal confession (al-qawl bi al-lisan) without requiring inner conviction. Nasafi cites the Qur'anic verse about the hypocrites, who say 'We believe' but are not believers, proving that inner tasdiq is a condition for the validity of iman. He then supports this with the hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) conditions entry into paradise on being 'sincere and pure' (khāliṣan mukhliṣan), indicating that sincerity (which includes inner affirmation) is required. Thus, the Karramiyya's position is refuted.

Key Terms
الكرامية
التصديق
شرط الإيمان
الاخلاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that simply saying the shahada makes one a believer, even without inner conviction.
Correction: The Quran and hadith show that verbal confession alone is insufficient; inner affirmation (tasdiq) is a necessary condition for iman.

Checkpoint

B) Karramiyya, using verse 2:8
C) Khawarij, using verse 14:31
D) Jahmiyya, using verse 5:6

Key Takeaway
Inner affirmation (tasdiq) is an indispensable condition for iman; mere verbal confession is insufficient.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you declare your faith in prayer or in daily life, do you ever pause to check if your inner state matches your words? What would it take for you to examine your heart's tasdiq right now?
?
The hypocrites spoke the same words of faith as believers, but Allah denied them iman. Is there any area of your life where your tongue claims belief but your heart is not fully convinced? Will you identify it and seek Allah's help to purify it?
?
The Prophet conditioned Paradise on sincerity and purity in saying 'la ilaha illallah'. If you were to be judged on the ikhlas (sincerity) of that declaration at this moment, would you be confident? What step will you take today to strengthen the conviction in your heart?

The Four Sectarian Views on Major Sin
Nasafi enumerates four sectarian positions on major sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the positions of the Khawarij, Murji'ah, Jabriyyah, and Mu'tazilah regarding a person who commits a major sin.

Core Idea
Different early sects had radically different views on the fate of a major sinner.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi introduces the core disagreement about the status of a Muslim who commits a grave sin. He lists the positions of four well-known sects, each with a distinct theological stance. Understanding these views is essential before evaluating the arguments for and against each.

Guided Path
1
Identify each sect's core claim
Read the passage and note what each sect says about a major sinner: does he become an unbeliever, remain a believer, or something else?
The Khawarij declare outright disbelief; the Murji'ah say sin doesn't harm faith; the Jabriyyah emphasize compulsion; the Mu'tazilah place the sinner in an intermediate state.
2
Reflect on the implications
Consider how each position affects the understanding of faith, accountability, and God's justice.
These differences lead to major debates about the definition of iman and the fate of sinful Muslims.
3
Memorize the Arabic terms
Note the key Arabic words for each sect and the phrase describing their view.
For example, 'كافر' (unbeliever) vs. 'يخرج من الإيمان ولا يدخل في الكفر' (exits faith but not enters disbelief).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان حكم مرتكب الكبيرة. قالت الخوارج لعنهم الله: من ارتكب الكبيرة يكفر. وقالوا: إن علياً رضي الله عنه كفر بقتل البغاة والخوارج. وقالت المرجئة: لا تضر المعصية مع الإيمان كما لا تنفع الطاعة مع الكفر. وقالت الجبرية: العباد مجبورون على الكفر والمعاصي. وقالت المعتزلة: يخرج بها من الإيمان ولا يدخل في الكفر. وشبهة الخوارج ظاهر الآية قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ تُطِيعُوهُمْ إِنَّكُمْ لَمُشْرِكُونَ﴾ [الأنعام: ١٢١] وقوله: ﴿وَمَنْ يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ وَيَتَعَدَّ حُدُودَهُ يُدْخِلْهُ نَارًا خَالِدًا فِيهَا﴾ والخلود إنما يكون لخروجه عن الإيمان، وكذلك قوله عليه السلام: لا يزني الزاني حين يزني وهو مؤمن، ولا يسرق السارق حين يسرق وهو مؤمن، ولا يشرب الشارب حين يشرب وهو مؤمن. وكذلك قوله عليه السلام: الصلاة عماد الدين فمن تركها فقد هدم الدين.
Chapter on explaining the ruling of the committer of a major sin. The Khawarij, may Allah curse them, said: Whoever commits a major sin becomes an unbeliever. And they said: Indeed, Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, became an unbeliever by killing the Baghah (rebels) and the Khawarij. And the Murji'ah said: Disobedience does not harm with faith just as obedience does not benefit with disbelief. And the Jabriyyah said: The servants are compelled to disbelief and sins. And the Mu'tazilah said: He exits by it from faith but does not enter into disbelief. And the proof (shubha) of the Khawarij is the apparent meaning of the verse, His statement the Exalted: 'And if you obey them, indeed you are polytheists' [al-An'am 121] and His statement: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger and transgresses His limits, He will admit him to a Fire, abiding therein eternally' — and eternity (khulud) is only due to exiting from faith. And likewise his saying, peace be upon him: 'The adulterer does not commit adultery while he is a believer, nor does the thief steal while he is a believer, nor does the drinker drink while he is a believer.' And likewise his saying, peace be upon him: 'Prayer is the pillar of religion; whoever abandons it has demolished religion.'
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the views of different Islamic sects regarding the ruling of a person who commits a major sin (kabira). The author lists the positions of the Khawarij (who declare such a person an unbeliever), the Murji'ah (who say sin does not harm faith), the Jabriyyah (who say humans are compelled), and the Mu'tazilah (who say the person is in a position between faith and disbelief). Then the author presents the proof (shubha) of the Khawarij, which is based on the apparent meaning of two Quranic verses and two hadiths. The first verse implies that obeying disbelievers makes one a polytheist, so committing a major sin is like obedience to them? Actually the verse is about obeying them, not about sin. The Khawarij interpret it broadly. The second verse threatens eternal punishment for those who disobey and transgress, which for them indicates that the person has left faith. The hadiths about the adulterer, thief, and drinker not being believers at the time of the act, and the hadith about prayer being the pillar, whose abandonment demolishes religion, are used to support the idea that major sins remove one from faith. However, the author does not provide the refutation in this passage; he only presents the views and the Khawarij's evidence. This sets up the subsequent discussion.

Key Terms
كبيرة
خوارج
مرجئة
جبرية
معتزلة
كفر
إيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Murji'ah
C) Jabriyyah
D) Mu'tazilah

Key Takeaway
The four main early Islamic sects—Khawarij, Murji'ah, Jabriyyah, and Mu'tazilah—each had a distinct position on the spiritual status of a major sinner, ranging from outright disbelief to an intermediate state.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Murji'ah said disobedience does not harm faith; do you ever use that as an excuse to downplay your sins? Where would your spiritual state be if you took obedience more seriously?

The Khawarij's Proofs from Quran and Hadith
Nasafi presents the Khawarij's scriptural evidence for takfir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will recognize the scriptural evidence the Khawarij used to support their view that major sinners become unbelievers, and understand why these texts were interpreted differently.

Core Idea
The Khawarij justified their harsh stance using apparent meanings of Quranic verses and prophetic hadith.

After presenting the four views, Imam Nasafi focuses on the Khawarij's proof. He quotes two Quranic verses and two hadiths that they interpreted as implying that major sins remove a person from faith. Examining these texts shows how the Khawarij derived their extreme position from sacred sources.

Guided Path
1
Read the verses and hadith
First, read the two Quranic verses and two hadiths quoted as evidence. Notice how each text is presented.
The first verse is about obeying disbelievers; the second threatens eternal punishment for disobedience. The hadiths speak about the adulterer, thief, drinker, and prayer.
2
Understand the Khawarij's reasoning
The Khawarij took these texts literally: they argued that eternal punishment (khalid) implies leaving faith, and that the hadiths imply a major sinner is not a believer at the moment of sin.
This connects to why they considered major sin as kufr.
3
Consider alternative interpretations
Think about how other sects might reinterpret these same texts. For example, the Murji'ah would say the hadiths refer to losing the full benefit of faith, not leaving it entirely.
The passage itself does not provide the refutation; it only presents the Khawarij's proof.

When you see a fellow Muslim commit a sin like drinking or stealing, does your heart immediately assume they have lost their faith? After reading this lesson, what will you do to check that assumption and respond with mercy instead?
?
The Khawarij used the apparent meaning of Quran 6:121 to label others polytheists. Are there areas in your life where you have judged someone's faith based on a single action without understanding their inner state? Write a specific step you will take to avoid this error.
?
The hadith about prayer being the pillar of religion is taken by the Khawarij to mean abandoning it destroys faith. Do you ever use similar logic to justify harshness toward those who neglect prayers? How can you balance warning with compassion from now on?

Views of Five Sects on the Major Sinner
Imam Nasafi enumerates the views of five sects on the major sinner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the divergent positions of five Islamic sects on the status of a person who commits a major sin.

Core Idea
The major sinner's fate depends on which sect you ask.

Imam Nasafi presents the views of five theological sects regarding the ruling on a Muslim who commits a major sin (kabirah). This passage surveys the extremes from declaring the sinner a disbeliever to claiming sin has no effect on faith, setting the stage for the Sunni position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the words of Imam Nasafi settle before you analyze.
The passage begins with a chapter heading.
2
Identify each sect and its view
Go through each of the five sects mentioned: Khawarij, Murji'a, Jabriyya, Mu'tazila. Write down their ruling on the major sinner in your own words.
Notice the progression from extreme to extreme.
3
Observe the logical extremes
Compare the views: Khawarij say the sinner becomes a disbeliever; Murji'a say sin has no effect; Jabriyya say compulsion; Mu'tazila say a middle state. Ask: which view seems too harsh, which too lenient?
4
Reflect on the missing Sunni position
Realize that this passage only lists deviant views. The correct Ahl al-Sunnah position is not given here—it will be defended later. Consider why it is important to know these errors first.
This is a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان حكم مرتكب الكبيرة
قالت الخوارج لعنهم الله: من ارتكب الكبيرة يَكْفُر. وقالوا: إن علياً رضي الله عنه كفَر بقتل البغاة والخوارج. وقالت المرجئة : لا تضر المعصية مع الإيمان كما لا تنفع الطاعة مع الكفر.
وقالت الجبرية: العباد مجبورون على الكفر والمعاصي.
وقالت المعتزلة: يخرج بها من الإيمان، ولا يدخل في الكفر.
Chapter on explaining the ruling on the committer of a major sin. The Khawarij (may Allah curse them) said: Whoever commits a major sin disbelieves. And they said: Indeed, Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) disbelieved by killing the rebels and the Khawarij. And the Murji'a said: Disobedience does not harm with faith just as obedience does not benefit with disbelief. And the Jabriyya said: The servants are compelled upon disbelief and sins. And the Mu'tazila said: He leaves faith by it, but does not enter disbelief.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a classification that presents the positions of five deviant sects regarding the ruling on the committer of a major sin (kabirah). It begins with the heading 'Chapter on explaining the ruling on the committer of a major sin.' Then it lists the views: The Khawarij hold that committing a major sin takes one out of Islam entirely into disbelief (kufr). They even accuse Ali (RA) of disbelief for fighting them. The Murji'a take the opposite extreme: that sin does not harm one's faith at all, just as obedience does not benefit a disbeliever. The Jabriyya deny human free will, claiming people are compelled (mujbarun) toward disbelief and sins. The Mu'tazila take a middle position: the major sinner leaves faith (iman) but does not enter disbelief; he is in a state between the two. This sets the stage for the Ahl al-Sunnah position, which is not listed here but will be defended later.

Misconception: This passage gives the correct Sunni position on the major sinner.
Correction: This passage only lists deviant views; the Sunni position is not stated here but will be presented later in the text.

Checkpoint

A) Khawarij
B) Murji'a
C) Mu'tazila
D) Jabriyya

Key Takeaway
The major sinner's status is a major point of sectarian division, with views ranging from outright disbelief to no effect, setting the stage for the Sunni middle path.

?

The Khawarij's Proof from Qur'an and Hadith
Imam Nasafi presents the Khawarij's proof from Qur'an and Hadith for takfir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Khawarij's scriptural arguments for declaring major sinners disbelievers.

Core Idea
The Khawarij misuse Qur'an and Hadith to justify takfir of sinners.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi presents the specious argument (shubha) of the Khawarij. They rely on apparent meanings of two Qur'anic verses and two prophetic hadiths to claim that committing major sins removes one from faith. Let's examine each proof and understand how they misinterpreted the texts.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation silently. Pay attention to the flow: first two verses, then two hadiths.
The passage lists four proofs: two from the Qur'an and two from the Sunnah.
2
Analyze the first verse proof
Look at Qur'an 6:121: 'if you obey them, you are polytheists.' The Khawarij take this literally to mean that obeying a sinful person makes one a polytheist. Ask yourself: is this verse about Muslims or about polytheists?
The full context of the verse addresses obeying polytheists, not believers.
3
Analyze the second verse proof
Qur'an 4:14 threatens eternal fire for those who disobey Allah and transgress His limits. The Khawarij argue that eternal punishment (khulud) implies leaving faith (iman). Consider: is eternal punishment always for disbelievers?
4
Examine the hadith proofs
The two hadiths: (1) 'No adulterer commits adultery while believing' and (2) 'Prayer is the pillar; abandoning it demolishes religion.' The Khawarij take these as evidence that sin negates faith. Notice that the first hadith is about the moment of sin, not the person's overall state.
The hadiths warn of severe consequences but do not declare the sinner a disbeliever.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشبهة الخوارج ظاهرُ الآية قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ أَطَعْتُمُوهُمْ إنَّكُمْ لَمَشْرِكُونَ ﴾ [الأنعا. ۱۲۱] وقوله: ﴿وَمَن يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ وَيَتَعَدَّ حُدُودَهُ يُدْخِلْهُ نَارًا خَلِدًا فِيهَا﴾ والخلود إنما يكون لخروجه عن الإيمان، وكذلك قوله عليه السلام: لا يزني الزاني حين يزني وهو مؤمن، ولا يسرق السارق حين يسرق وهو مؤمن، ولا يشرب الشارب حين يشرب وهو مؤمن. وكذا قوله عليه السلام: الصلاة عماد الدين فمن تركها فقد هدم الدين.
And the doubt of the Khawarij is the apparent meaning of the verse, the saying of the Exalted: 'And if you obey them, indeed you are polytheists' [al-An'am 121], and His saying: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger and transgresses His limits, He will cause him to enter fire, abiding therein forever,' and eternity is only due to his leaving faith, and likewise his saying (peace be upon him): 'The adulterer does not commit adultery while he is a believer, and the thief does not steal while he is a believer, and the drinker does not drink while he is a believer.' And likewise his saying (peace be upon him): 'Prayer is the pillar of religion; whoever abandons it has demolished religion.'
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage presents the shubha (specious argument) of the Khawarij. They base their claim that a major sinner becomes a disbeliever on apparent meanings of Qur'anic verses and prophetic hadiths. First, they cite the verse 'And if you obey them, indeed you are polytheists' (6:121), taking it literally to mean that any obedience to sinful people amounts to shirk. Second, they cite 'Whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger and transgresses His limits, He will cause him to enter fire, abiding therein forever' (4:14), arguing that eternal punishment (khulud) in fire is only for those who have left faith (iman). Third, they cite the famous hadith: 'The adulterer does not commit adultery while he is a believer...' which seems to negate faith at the moment of sin. Fourth, they cite the hadith 'Prayer is the pillar of religion; whoever abandons it has demolished religion,' implying that abandoning prayer destroys one's faith entirely. Thus they conclude that major sins nullify iman.

Key Terms
شبهة
خلود
إيمان
كبيرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Khawarij think that the verses and hadiths they cite prove that any major sinner is a disbeliever.
Correction: The verses are taken out of context (6:121 is about obeying polytheists, not Muslims) or misinterpreted (4:14 does not specify that every sinner will be eternal). The hadiths negate faith at the moment of sin but do not remove one from the fold of Islam entirely.

Checkpoint
Which verse do the Khawarij use to argue that the major sinner will be eternally punished?
A) وَإِنْ أَطَعْتُمُوهُمْ إِنَّكُمْ لَمَشْرِكُونَ
B) وَمَن يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ وَيَتَعَدَّ حُدُودَهُ يُدْخِلْهُ نَارًا خَلِدًا فِيهَا
C) يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا تُوبُوا إِلَى اللَّهِ تَوْبَةً نَصُوحًا
D) الصَّلَاةُ عِمَادُ الدِّينِ

Key Takeaway
The Khawarij erroneously interpret verses about eternal punishment and hadiths about removal of faith at the moment of sin as evidence that a major sinner leaves Islam entirely.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever read a verse or hadith that made you feel justified in condemning someone else's sin? How does the Khawarij's error warn you about the danger of interpreting texts without proper context, especially when it leads you to look down on others?
?
The hadith says 'no zina while believing' – when you think of your own sins, do you fear that they have diminished your faith? Does this lesson give you hope that your iman remains intact despite your shortcomings, and how should that affect your repentance?
?
The Khawarij used the threat of eternal punishment to declare others disbelievers. Have you ever used the fear of Hell to control or judge others rather than to humble yourself before Allah? How can you redirect that fear to self-accountability and reliance on Allah's mercy?

The Ahl al-Sunnah Proof from Repentance and Prayer Behind Sinners
Imam Nasafi presents two Qur'anic verses and a hadith as proof that major sins do not remove faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunnah proof that believers remain believers despite major sins, based on the command to repent and the hadith about prayer behind every person.

Core Idea
Repentance and prayer behind sinners prove believers remain believers.

Imam Nasafi begins by presenting two clear proofs from the Qur'an and Sunnah that establish the Ahl al-Sunnah position. He first cites the verses commanding all believers to repent, which presupposes they sin, and then the hadith instructing prayer behind every person—including the sinful—which would not be commanded if sin removed faith entirely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully, noticing the structure: two Qur'anic verses followed by a hadith, each presented as proof.
2
Analyze the repentance verses
Examine how the two verses command believers to repent. Note that repentance is from sin, and the text says repentance is from major sin (kabirah). This implies that believers can commit major sins.
3
Understand the hadith
The hadith commands praying behind every pious and sinful person. If a major sinner had left faith, the Prophet (PBUH) would not have ordered it because prayer behind a non-believer is invalid.
This is a logical deduction.
4
Connect to the conclusion
These evidences together prove that major sins do not expel faith. The believer who sins is still a believer, though sinful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحجتنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَتُوبُوا إِلَى اللَّهِ جَمِيعًا أَيُّهَ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ لَعَلَّكُمْ تُفْلِحُونَ ﴾ [النور: ۳۱] وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿يَاأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا تُوبُوا إِلَى اللَّهِ تَوْبَةً نَصُوحًا ﴾ [التحريم: ۸] والتوبة إنما تكون من الخوبة وهى الكبيرة. وكذلك قوله عليه السلام: صَلُّوا خلف كل بر وفاجره فلو خرج من الإيمان لما أَمَرَ بالصلاة خلفه. وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ أَطَعْتُمُوهُمْ إِنَّكُمْ لَمَشْرِكُونَ ﴾ [الأنعام: ١١٢] قلنا: المراد به الطاعة في الشرك؛ لأنهم قالوا: الميتة حلال؛ لأنه مذبوح الله تعالى، فأنزل الله تعالى هذه الآية: وَلَا تَأْكُلُوا مِمَّا لَمْ يُذكر أسْمُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ ﴾ [الأنعام: ۱۱۲] وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ وَيَتَعَدَّ حُدُودَهُ يُدْخِلْهُ نَارًا خَلِدًا فِيهَا ﴾ قلنا: المراد منه الكفار، لأن التعدي إنما يكون من الكفار. وأما قوله عليه السلام: لا يزني الزاني حين يزني وهو مؤمن.
And our proof is the saying of the Exalted: 'And turn in repentance to Allah all together, O believers, that you may succeed' [al-Nur 31], and likewise the saying of the Exalted: 'O you who have believed, repent to Allah with sincere repentance' [al-Tahrim 8], and repentance is only from sin, and it is the major sin. And likewise his saying (peace be upon him): 'Pray behind every pious and sinful person,' for if he had left faith, he would not have commanded prayer behind him. As for the saying of the Exalted: 'And if you obey them, indeed you are polytheists' [al-An'am 112], we say: what is meant by it is obedience in polytheism; because they said: carrion is lawful because it is slaughtered by Allah, so Allah revealed this verse: 'And do not eat of that upon which the name of Allah has not been mentioned' [al-An'am 112]. And as for the saying of the Exalted: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger and transgresses His limits, He will cause him to enter fire, abiding therein forever,' we say: what is meant by it is the disbelievers, because transgression is only from the disbelievers. And as for his saying (peace be upon him): 'The adulterer does not commit adultery while he is a believer.'
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage presents the proof (hujjah) of Ahl al-Sunnah and then refutes the three main evidences of the Khawarij. It begins by citing two Qur'anic verses that command believers to repent (tawbah) from sin, specifically major sins (kabirah). Since repentance is only from sin, this proves that believers can commit major sins while remaining believers; otherwise, repentance would be meaningless. Then it cites the hadith commanding prayer behind every person, whether pious or sinful (fajir). If the major sinner had left faith, the Prophet would not have ordered us to pray behind him. Next, it refutes the Khawarij's first verse about obedience leading to shirk: it clarifies that this verse refers to obedience in actual polytheism, not obedience in sin. The context was the pagans claiming that carrion was lawful because it was 'slaughtered by Allah' (meaning natural death). The second verse about eternal punishment is interpreted as referring to disbelievers (kuffar), not Muslims, because transgression of limits in that severe sense is characteristic of disbelief. As for the hadith about the adulterer not being a believer, the text begins to answer but stops; however, the implied answer is that this hadith is understood as a warning or as negating perfect faith, not faith itself. This demonstrates the Ahl al-Sunnah methodology of interpreting ambiguous texts in light of clear proofs.

Key Terms
توبة
كبيرة
بر وفاجر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that any major sin expels a person from Islam entirely, making them a kafir.
Correction: This passage shows that believers are commanded to repent from major sins, and prayer behind sinners is ordered, proving they remain believers.

Checkpoint
What is the logical implication of the hadith 'Pray behind every pious and sinful person'?
A) It means that all people are equally sinful.
B) It proves that sinful people are still believers.
C) It commands us to avoid praying with sinners.
D) It shows that sinless people are the only true believers.

Key Takeaway
The command to repent from major sins and the order to pray behind sinners confirm that major sins do not expel faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

How does this lesson's truth—that your sin does not remove you from faith—reshape your willingness to serve the community? Will you let shame keep you from fulfilling duties, or will you step forward in humility?

Refuting the Khawarij Evidences on Sin and Disbelief
Imam Nasafi refutes three Khawarij evidences regarding sin leading to disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ahl al-Sunnah refutes three key Khawarij proofs from the Qur'an and hadith that claim major sinners leave faith.

Core Idea
The Khawarij misinterpret verses; obedience to sin is not shirk, and eternal punishment is for disbelievers.

After presenting his own proof, Imam Nasafi addresses the Khawarij's evidences. They cite verses about obedience leading to shirk, eternal punishment for transgressors, and a hadith about the adulterer not being a believer. Nasafi provides clear refutations by contextualizing the verses and explaining the hadith's meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutations
Read the Arabic passage covering the three refutations. Notice the pattern: each Khawarij evidence is introduced by 'As for the saying...' and then refuted with 'We say...'.
2
Analyze the first refutation
The verse about obeying polytheists leading to shirk is explained: it refers to obedience in polytheism, not obedience in sin. The context is about carrion.
3
Analyze the second refutation
The verse about eternal punishment for those who disobey and transgress limits is said to refer to disbelievers, not believers.
Transgression in that severe sense is characteristic of kufr.
4
Understand the third
The hadith 'No adulterer commits adultery while a believer' is started but not fully answered here; the implied answer is that it negates perfect faith or is a warning.
5
Synthesize
Recognize the Ahl al-Sunnah method: ambiguous texts are interpreted in light of clear proofs, not taken literally to contradict established principles.

And our proof is the saying of the Exalted: 'And turn in repentance to Allah all together, O believers, that you may succeed' [al-Nur 31], and likewise the saying of the Exalted: 'O you who have believed, repent to Allah with sincere repentance' [al-Tahrim 8], and repentance is only from sin, and it is the major sin. Checkpoint
According to Imam Nasafi, who is the verse about eternal punishment for those who disobey Allah and His Messenger referring to?
A) All sinners
B) Disbelievers
C) Polytheists
D) Believers who commit major sins

Key Takeaway
The Khawarij verses are misapplied; proper interpretation shows that major sins do not expel faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you quick to label someone's sin as a sign of weak faith or even disbelief? How does this lesson's insistence on interpreting verses in their proper context challenge your judgment of others?
?
When you fall into a major sin, do you sometimes feel that your faith is completely broken? How can the distinction between sin and disbelief—so carefully drawn by Imam Nasafi—change how you approach tawbah?
?
Think of a sin you have normalized in your life, perhaps by saying 'it's not that serious' or 'everyone does it.' How does the Khawarij error of over-correcting remind you that the right balance is to see sin as serious but not faith-destroying? What will you do to take that sin more seriously today?
