Refuting the Claim of Imam Ali's Return
Imam Nasafi refutes extremist Shia belief in Ali's return using the manzila hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the analogy between Ali and Aaron does not support the Shia belief in Imam Ali's return, and how contextual interpretation resolves the apparent argument.

Core Idea
Context explains the 'manzila' hadith; Aaron's death before Moses disproves permanent succession.

Extremist Shia groups have used the famous hadith in which the Prophet compared Ali to Aaron to argue that Ali will return after death, just as Aaron's succession to Moses was uninterrupted. Imam Nasafi refutes this by examining the historical context and the logic of the analogy. In this lesson, we will unpack his argument and see why the comparison actually undermines the claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the hadith cited
Begin by reading the objection that the Shia present: the Prophet said to Ali, 'You are to me as Aaron was to Moses,' and they argue this implies a permanent succession without alteration.
The hadith is authentic, but its interpretation is contested.
2
Understand the Shia interpretation
The Shia claim that since Aaron's succession to Moses was permanent and continued after Moses' death (as per their belief), Ali's succession should also be permanent, implying his return after his apparent death.
3
See how Imam Nasafi recontextualizes the hadith
Imam Nasafi explains that the hadith was said in a specific context: when the Prophet left Ali in charge of Medina while he went to battle, and hypocrites accused the Prophet of abandoning Ali. The Prophet's words were meant to console Ali, not to establish a general principle of succession.
This directly refutes the Shia interpretation.
4
Grasp the key point: Aaron died before Moses
The analogy with Aaron actually weakens the Shia claim because Aaron died before Moses, so his succession ended before Moses' death. If the Prophet intended to indicate succession after his own death, he would have compared Ali to Joshua, who succeeded Moses and lived after him.
5
Recognize the alternative analogy with Joshua
Imam Nasafi points out that the correct analogy for post-death succession would be Joshua, not Aaron. Since the Prophet did not use that analogy, the hadith cannot be used to prove Ali's return.
This is the final nail in the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الرد على غلاة الشيعة القائلين بعودة الإمام علي عليه السلام فإن قيل: رُوِيَ عن النبي أنه قال لعلي رضي الله عنه: «أنت مني بمنزلة هارون من موسى عليه السلام إلا أنه لا نبي بعدي » (۱) وخلافة هارون لم يكن لها تبديل فكذلك ههنا. والجواب عنه أن نقول: فضيلته لم تكن من الوجه الذي توهمتم لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم استخلفه على المدينة وخرج إلى بعض الغزوات، فقال المنافقون: النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أعرض عنه وحبسه في البيت، فاغتم بذلك علي رضي الله عنه، فقال له النبي عليه السلام: «أنت مني بمنزلة هارون من موسى عليه السلام يدل عليه أنَّ هارون مات قبل موسى عليه السلام، وإنما يصح هذا أن لو قال: أنت مني بمنزلة يوشع بن نون عليه السلام، وقد كان خليفة موسى عليه السلام [يومين] (٢).
Chapter on refuting the extremists among the Shia who claim the return of Imam Ali, peace be upon him. For it is said: It is narrated from the Prophet that he said to Ali, may Allah be pleased with him: 'You are to me as Aaron was to Moses, peace be upon him, except that there is no prophet after me' (1). And the succession of Aaron had no alteration, so likewise here. The answer to that is that we say: His virtue was not in the way you imagined, because the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, appointed him as deputy over Medina and went out to some battles. Then the hypocrites said: 'The Prophet has turned away from him and confined him in the house.' Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, became distressed by that, so the Prophet, peace be upon him, said to him: 'You are to me as Aaron was to Moses, peace be upon him.' This indicates that Aaron died before Moses, peace be upon him. And this would only be correct if he had said: 'You are to me as Joshua son of Nun, peace be upon him,' and he was the successor of Moses, peace be upon him, for [two days] (2).
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a specific claim made by extremist Shia who believe that Imam Ali will return (raj'a). The objection presents a hadith where the Prophet likens Ali to Aaron, arguing that since Aaron's succession to Moses was permanent and without change, Ali's succession should also be permanent, implying his return after death. The answer refutes this by explaining that the hadith was said in a specific context: when the Prophet left Ali in charge of Medina during a battle, and hypocrites accused the Prophet of abandoning Ali. The Prophet's statement was meant to console Ali, not to establish a permanent succession. Moreover, the analogy with Aaron is imperfect because Aaron died before Moses, so his succession ended. If the Prophet intended to indicate succession after his death, he would have compared Ali to Joshua, who succeeded Moses and lived after him. Thus, the hadith does not support the claim of Ali's return.

Key Terms
غلاة الشيعة
عودة الإمام علي
هارون من موسى
يوشع بن نون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Shia belief that the manzila hadith proves Imam Ali will physically return after death because Aaron's succession was permanent.
Correction: The hadith was a contextual consolation; Aaron died before Moses, so his succession was not post-death. The correct analogy for succession after death is Joshua, not Aaron.

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Nasafi argue that the analogy with Aaron does not prove Imam Ali's return?
A) Because Aaron never died, so the analogy is invalid.
B) Because Aaron died before Moses, so his succession ended; true succession after death would require an analogy with Joshua.
C) Because the hadith is weak and not authentic.
D) Because the Prophet meant that Ali is like Aaron only in virtue, not in succession.

Key Takeaway
The hadith comparing Ali to Aaron was a contextual consolation, not an endorsement of permanent succession; the correct analogy for succession after death is with Joshua.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The extremists clung to a hadith despite clear contextual evidence that it meant something else. Is there a religious conviction you hold so tightly that you ignore contextual or historical evidence? What would it take for you to reconsider it today?
?
The Prophet's words to Ali were a tailored consolation for a specific moment. Is there a person in your life whom you need to console with words suited to their situation, rather than offering generic advice? What will you say to them this week?
?
The correct analogy would have been Joshua, but the Prophet chose Aaron. Are you willing to accept that the Prophet's words were perfectly appropriate for their context, even if it means giving up a cherished interpretation? What cherished belief are you ready to surrender to follow the Prophet more closely?

Refuting extreme Shia claims about Imam Ali
Imam Nasafi refutes three extreme Shia claims about Imam Ali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni refutation of extreme Shia claims about revelation and knowledge attributed to Imam Ali, and why they are considered disbelief.

Core Idea
Claims that Ali received revelation or surpassed the Prophet contradict the Qur'an and consensus.

Imam Nasafi addresses three extreme Shia positions regarding Imam Ali: that he received revelation (with Gabriel's error), that he was a partner in prophethood, and that he was more knowledgeable than the Prophet. Each is refuted using the Qur'an, consensus, and the Prophet's own words.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Identify the three distinct claims being refuted by Imam Nasafi.
The claims are about revelation, partnership in prophethood, and superior knowledge.
2
Understand why disbelief
For the first two claims, note the reason: they deny the clear Qur'anic text and consensus that Muhammad is the final messenger.
The verse from al-Fath is cited as evidence.
3
Analyze the third claim and answer
The third claim is about Ali's superior knowledge. The answer uses the hadith 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate' to show Ali's knowledge comes from the Prophet.
The logic: a gate cannot be greater than the city.
4
Reflect on the lesson's core idea
Why is it important to defend the Prophet's exclusive prophethood? This protects the foundational belief of Islam.
These refutations safeguard the finality of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الرد على من قال بأن الإمام عليا عليه السلام يوحى إليه وصِنْفُ من الروافض قالوا بأنَّ الوحي كان لعليَّ رَضِيَ الله عنه، إلا أنَّ جبرائيل عليه السلام غلط في الوحي. وصِنْفٌ منهم قالوا بأنه كان شريكا في النبوة، وهؤلاء كلهم كفَّارٌ، لأنهم أنكروا نص القرآن وإجماع الأمة، قال الله تعالى: ﴿مُحَمَّدٌ رَّسُولُ اللَّهِ﴾ [الفتح: ٢٩]. وبعضهم قالوا: إن عليا رضي الله عنه كان أعلم من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو بمنزلة الخضر من موسى. والجواب عنه أن نقول: ذلك العِلْمُ كان له بتعليم النبي بقوله عليه السلام: «أنا مدينة العلم وعلى بابها » والباب لا يكون أعظم من المدينة.
Chapter on refuting those who say that Imam Ali, peace be upon him, received revelation. And a group of the Rawafid said that revelation was to Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, except that Gabriel, peace be upon him, made a mistake in the revelation. And another group among them said that he was a partner in prophethood. All of these are disbelievers, because they denied the clear text of the Qur'an and the consensus of the community. Allah Almighty said: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' (al-Fath 48:29). And some of them said that Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, was more knowledgeable than the Prophet, peace be upon him, and that he is like al-Khidr to Moses. The answer to that is that we say: That knowledge was his through the teaching of the Prophet, by his statement, peace be upon him: 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate.' And the gate is not greater than the city.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage refutes various extreme Shia claims regarding revelation and knowledge attributed to Imam Ali. The author identifies two groups: one claims that revelation was sent to Ali but Gabriel made a mistake in delivering it; another claims that Ali was a partner in prophethood. Both are declared disbelievers (kuffar) because they contradict the explicit Qur'anic verse 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' and the consensus (ijma) of the Muslim community that Muhammad is the final prophet. Additionally, a third claim is that Ali was more knowledgeable than the Prophet, comparing him to al-Khidr who had knowledge beyond Moses. The answer refutes this by citing the hadith 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate,' arguing that a gate is not greater than the city itself. Thus, Ali's knowledge came from the Prophet's teaching, and he cannot surpass the Prophet in knowledge.

Correction: The hadith actually shows that Ali's knowledge is from the Prophet; a gate is part of and lesser than the city.

Checkpoint

A) Because they deny the prophethood of Muhammad.

C) Because they claim Ali is more knowledgeable than the Prophet.
D) Because they believe in the return of Ali.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet Muhammad is the final messenger and the source of all religious knowledge; no one can surpass him in prophethood or knowledge.

The Rafidi Claims About Revelation to Ali
Nasafi declares two Rafidi claims about revelation and prophethood as kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi declares the Rafidi claims about Ali receiving revelation or sharing prophethood as kufr, based on Quranic text and consensus.

Core Idea
Denying Muhammad's exclusive prophethood is kufr, regardless of how it is dressed up.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi addresses two extremist Shia (Rafidi) claims: that revelation was sent to Ali but Jibril mistakenly delivered it to Muhammad, and that Ali was a partner in prophethood. He categorically declares both as disbelief, grounding his ruling in the clear Quranic verse 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' and the consensus of the Muslim community.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Let the author's own words come through.
Notice how concisely Nasafi states the claims and ruling.
2
Identify the two Rafidi claims
The passage presents two distinct claims: the first involves Jibril's alleged error, the second involves partnership in prophethood. Identify both.
3
Understand why they constitute kufr
Nasafi declares both groups as disbelievers because they deny the text of the Quran and the consensus of the community. Reflect on why denial of these two sources is so serious.
The Quran verse 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' is central.
4
Reflect on the role of Quranic text and ijma
Consider how Nasafi uses the Quran and ijma as the sole basis for takfir. This illustrates a key method in kalam: rulings are derived from revealed sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الرد على من قال بأن الإمام عليا عليه السلام يوحى إليه وصِنْفُ من الروافض قالوا بأنَّ الوحي كان لعليَّ رَضِيَ الله عنه، إلا أنَّ جبرائيل عليه السلام غلط في الوحي. وصِنْفٌ منهم قالوا بأنه كان شريكا في النبوة، وهؤلاء كلهم كفَّارٌ، لأنهم أنكروا نص القرآن وإجماع الأمة، قال الله تعالى: ﴿مُحَمَّدٌ رَّسُولُ اللَّهِ﴾ [الفتح: ٢٩]. وبعضهم قالوا: إن عليا رضي الله عنه كان أعلم من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو بمنزلة الخضر من موسى. والجواب عنه أن نقول: ذلك العِلْمُ كان له بتعليم النبي بقوله عليه السلام: «أنا مدينة العلم وعلى بابها» والباب لا يكون أعظم من المدينة. يدل عليه أن عليا رضي الله عنه كان وليّا، والرسول عليه السّلام كان نبياً، ولا شك أن النبي أفضل من الولي، وأما الخضر كان له علمٌ لَدُنِّي بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَعَلَّمْنَاهُ مِن لَدُنَّا عِلْمًا﴾ [الكهف: ٦٥] وأراد به علم الإلهام، وموسى عليه السلام أفضل؛ لأنه صاحب شريعة وله كتاب، وصاحب الكتاب والشّريعة أفضل كداود مع سلیمان عليهما السلام فداود أفضل لأنه أنزل عليه الزبور.
Chapter on refuting those who say that Imam Ali (peace be upon him) receives revelation. And a group of the Rafidah said that revelation was to Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), except that Jibril (peace be upon him) erred in the revelation. And a group of them said that he was a partner in prophethood. These all are disbelievers, because they denied the text of the Quran and the consensus of the community. Allah Most High said: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' [Al-Fath: 29]. And some of them said that Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) was more knowledgeable than the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) and that he was in the position of Khidr to Moses. The answer to that is that we say: That knowledge was his by the teaching of the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) by his statement: 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate,' and the gate is not greater than the city. This is supported by the fact that Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) was a saint (wali), and the Messenger (peace be upon him) was a prophet (nabi), and there is no doubt that the prophet is superior to the saint. As for Khidr, he had knowledge from Our Presence (ladunni) by the saying of Allah Most High: 'And We taught him from Our Presence knowledge' [Al-Kahf: 65], meaning knowledge of inspiration (ilm al-ilham). And Moses (peace be upon him) is superior because he was a possessor of a law (shari'a) and had a book. And the possessor of a book and a law is superior, like David with Solomon (peace be upon them) — David is superior because the Psalms (Zabur) were revealed to him.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of extremist Shia (Rafidi) claims about Imam Ali. The author first describes two Rafidi claims: (1) that revelation was sent to Ali but Jibril mistakenly delivered it to Muhammad, and (2) that Ali was a partner in prophethood. Nasafi declares both claims as kufr (disbelief) because they deny the clear Quranic text (Surah Al-Fath: 29) that explicitly calls Muhammad the Messenger of Allah, and they contradict the consensus (ijma) of the Muslim community. He then addresses a third claim: that Ali was more knowledgeable than the Prophet and comparable to Khidr in relation to Moses. The response is twofold. First, the author argues that Ali's knowledge came from the Prophet's teaching, using the hadith (though its authenticity is debated among scholars) that the Prophet is the city of knowledge and Ali its gate. Since a gate is not greater than the city, Ali cannot be greater than the Prophet. Second, the author makes a general principle: a prophet (nabi) is superior to a saint (wali), and Ali was a wali while the Prophet was a nabi. Then he addresses the analogy of Khidr and Moses: Khidr had ladunni (direct divine) knowledge, which is knowledge of inspiration (ilham), but Moses was superior because he was a prophet with a scripture (the Torah) and a law (shari'a). The author notes that having a book and a shari'a makes a prophet superior, citing the example of David and Solomon — both were prophets, but David is considered superior because the Zabur was revealed to him. Thus, the claim that Ali was like Khidr and more knowledgeable is refuted. The author concludes that the Prophet Muhammad is superior to all, and the Rafidi claims are baseless denial of clear texts and consensus.

Key Terms
الروافض
الوحي
النبوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that claiming Ali received revelation is acceptable as long as Muhammad is still the final prophet.
Correction: Nasafi shows that any claim that denies the exclusive prophethood of Muhammad, even by alleging an error by Jibril, is kufr because it contradicts the clear Quranic text and consensus.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi declare the Rafidi claims about Ali receiving revelation as kufr?
A) Because they contradict the consensus of the companions.
B) Because they deny the clear Quranic text and the consensus of the community.
C) Because they claim Ali was a partner in prophethood, which is impossible.
D) Because they say Jibril erred, which is an insult to the angels.

Key Takeaway
Any claim that denies the exclusive prophethood of Muhammad, whether by alleging an error by Jibril or sharing prophethood, is kufr because it contradicts the Quran and ijma.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read the verse 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' again. Do you truly hold this in your heart as an absolute, exclusive truth? If someone today said that a saint or leader could share in prophethood, would you feel the same sense of violation as if they denied Allah? Ask yourself: is there any person I have elevated in my mind to a status that competes with the Prophet's finality? Repent and renew your conviction.
?
The Rafidis claimed Jibril made a mistake. Have you ever doubted the reliability of the Quran's transmission because of some report or story? If you have, what does that say about your trust in Allah's preservation of His revelation? This lesson demands that we see any such doubt as a serious breach of iman. Examine your thoughts carefully.
?
Nasafi declared these Rafidis disbelievers because they denied the Quran and ijma. When you encounter a sectarian claim that contradicts clear Quranic texts, do you boldly uphold the truth, or do you compromise to avoid conflict? How does your response reflect your love for Allah and His Messenger? Make a firm intention to defend the uniqueness of Muhammad ﷺ in your words and actions.

The Rafidi Claim of Ali's Superior Knowledge and the Khidr Analogy
Nasafi refutes the claim that Ali was more knowledgeable than the Prophet using hadith and the superiority of prophets over saints.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the claim that Ali was more knowledgeable than the Prophet and the analogy of Khidr and Moses, using the city-gate hadith and the principle of prophetic superiority.

Core Idea
A prophet is always superior to a saint, and Ali's knowledge came from the Prophet, not independently.

Nasafi now addresses a more subtle Rafidi claim: that Ali was more knowledgeable than the Prophet and comparable to Khidr in relation to Moses. To refute this, he uses the famous (though debated) hadith 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate' to show that Ali's knowledge is derived from the Prophet, and then establishes a general principle that prophets are superior to saints, even if the saint has ladunni knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the claim about Ali's knowledge
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the structure: claim, then two counter-arguments, then the Khidr-Musa analogy.
2
Understand the use of the hadith 'city of knowledge'
Nasafi uses the hadith to show that Ali's knowledge is derivative, not independent. The gate is part of the city, not greater than it.
The authenticity of this hadith is debated among scholars, but Nasafi uses it as known to his audience.
3
Compare the roles of nabi and wali
Nasafi states a clear principle: a prophet (nabi) is superior to a saint (wali). Identify why this is foundational for his argument.
4
Analyze the Khidr-Moses analogy
Nasafi explains that Khidr's knowledge was ladunni (direct divine inspiration), but Moses was superior because he had a shari'a and a book. Consider why having a book and law elevates a prophet.
The example of David and Solomon reinforces the point.
5
Reflect on the overall refutation
Synthesize: the Rafidi claim is refuted on two levels — derivative knowledge and the inherent superiority of prophets.

فصل في الرد على من قال بأن الإمام عليا عليه السلام يوحى إليه وصِنْفُ من الروافض قالوا بأنَّ الوحي كان لعليَّ رَضِيَ الله عنه، إلا أنَّ جبرائيل عليه السلام غلط في الوحي. وصِنْفٌ منهم قالوا بأنه كان شريكا في النبوة، وهؤلاء كلهم كفَّارٌ، لأنهم أنكروا نص القرآن وإجماع الأمة، قال الله تعالى: ﴿مُحَمَّدٌ رَّسُولُ اللَّهِ﴾ [الفتح: ٢٩]. وبعضهم قالوا: إن عليا رضي الله عنه كان أعلم من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو بمنزلة الخضر من موسى. والجواب عنه أن نقول: ذلك العِلْمُ كان له بتعليم النبي بقوله عليه السلام: «أنا مدينة العلم وعلى بابها» والباب لا يكون أعظم من المدينة. يدل عليه أن عليا رضي الله عنه كان وليّا، والرسول عليه السّلام كان نبياً، ولا شك أن النبي أفضل من الولي، وأما الخضر كان له علمٌ لَدُنِّي بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَعَلَّمْنَاهُ مِن لَدُنَّا عِلْمًا﴾ [الكهف: ٦٥] وأراد به علم الإلهام، وموسى عليه السلام أفضل؛ لأنه صاحب شريعة وله كتاب، وصاحب الكتاب والشّريعة أفضل كداود مع سلیمان عليهما السلام فداود أفضل لأنه أنزل عليه الزبور.
Chapter on refuting those who say that Imam Ali (peace be upon him) receives revelation. And a group of the Rafidah said that revelation was to Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), except that Jibril (peace be upon him) erred in the revelation. And a group of them said that he was a partner in prophethood. These all are disbelievers, because they denied the text of the Quran and the consensus of the community. Commentary
This passage is a refutation of extremist Shia (Rafidi) claims about Imam Ali. Refuting the Return of Imam Ali (Raj'ah)
Nasafi refutes the Shia Ghulat belief in raj'ah with three proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni stance on the return of the dead and the scriptural proofs that refute the Shia Ghulat belief in raj'ah.

Core Idea
No one returns to this world after death until the Day of Resurrection.

This passage confronts a specific sectarian claim: that Imam Ali and his companions will return to this world before the final day to establish justice. Nasafi presents the Sunni position that death is a final departure, supported by the Quran and hadith. As you read, notice how each proof directly counters the idea of a pre-resurrection return.

Guided Path
1
Read the claim and the Sunni response
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to how Nasafi states the Shia claim and then the Sunni position. Notice the key phrase 'لا يرجع إلى الدنيا'.
The Shia claim includes a specific purpose: vengeance and justice.
2
Identify the three proofs
The author gives three proofs: two from the Quran and one from the Prophet. Find each proof and note how they are introduced.
The first proof is from Surah Taha, the second from Surah Ya Sin, and the third is a hadith.
3
Analyze the first proof (Taha 55)
Examine the verse 'From it We created you...' and the author's comment that Allah did not say 'twice'. What does this imply about the number of returns to the earth?
The verse mentions one return (into the earth) and one bringing out (on resurrection day).
4
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how the three proofs together form a cumulative case. Why does the hadith about 'only Paradise or Hell' after death complete the refutation?
If after death there is only the afterlife, there can be no return to worldly life.

فصل في الرد على غلاة الشيعة القائلين بعودة الإمام علي عليه السلام] وصنف من الروافض قالوا: إنَّ عليا رضي الله عنه وأصحابه يرجعون إلى الدنيا فينتقمون من أعدائهم فيملأ الأرض عدلاً كما ملنتْ جَوْرًا وظلمًا. وقال أهل السنة والجماعة كلّ من مات لا يرجع إلى الدنيا إلى يوم القيامة؛ لأنه لا يُقام الدليل عليه. ويدل على صحة ما قلنا قوله تعالى: مِنْهَا خَلَقْتَكُم وَفِيهَا نُعِيدُكُمْ وَمِنْهَا تُخْرِجُكُمْ تَارَةً أُخرى ﴾ [طه: ٥٥] ولم يقل مرتين، وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿أَلَمْ يَرَوْا كَمْ أَهْلَكْنَا قَبْلَهُم مِن الْقُرُونِ أَنَّهُمْ إِلَيْهِمْ لَا يَرْجِعُونَ ﴾ [يس: ۳۱] وكذلك قوله عليه السلام: «ليس بعد الموت إلا الجنة والنار».
Chapter on refuting the extremist Shia who claim the return of Imam Ali (peace be upon him). And a group of the Rawafid said: Indeed Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) and his companions will return to this world and take revenge from their enemies and fill the earth with justice as it had been filled with tyranny and oppression. And the Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah said: Everyone who dies does not return to this world until the Day of Resurrection, because no proof is established for it. And what proves the correctness of what we said is the saying of Allah Most High: 'From it (the earth) We created you, and into it We will return you, and from it We will bring you out another time' [Taha 55] and He did not say twice, as well as His saying: 'Have they not seen how many generations We destroyed before them? They will not return to them' [Ya Sin 31], and likewise his saying (peace be upon him): 'After death there is only Paradise or Hellfire.'
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Ghulat (extremist) Shia belief in raj'ah (return). It begins by stating the claim of a group of Rawafid that Ali and his companions will return to this world to exact vengeance and establish justice. Then it presents the Sunni position: no one returns to this world after death until the Day of Judgment. The author gives three proofs: 1) Quran 20:55 which says 'into it We will return you' (singular) and 'from it We will bring you out another time'—not twice. 2) Quran 36:31 which says the destroyed generations will not return to them. 3) A hadith that after death there is only Paradise or Hell. All these prove there is no return to worldly life.

Correction: This belief is held only by the Ghulat (extremist) Shia, not mainstream Shia. Nasafi refutes it with clear Quranic and hadith evidence.

Refuting the Return of the Dead
Refutes Shi'a belief in the return of Imam Ali and his companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the return of the dead (raj'a) and the scriptural proofs used to refute the Shi'a belief.

Core Idea
The dead do not return to this world; after death awaits only resurrection.

This lesson addresses a contentious theological issue: the belief held by some Shi'a groups that Imam Ali and his companions will return to this world before the Day of Judgment. The author, Imam Nasafi, presents the Sunni stance and provides clear Quranic and hadith evidence. As you read, notice how each proof directly counters the claim of a pre-resurrection return.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Shi'a claim
Read the claim of the Rawafid that Imam Ali and his companions will return to take revenge and establish justice.
2
Identify the Sunni response
Note the Sunni position: no one returns to this world after death until resurrection, and why there is no proof.
3
Examine the first proof from the Quran
Reflect on verse 20:55 and its implication that there is only one return (resurrection), not multiple.
Allah says 'another time' not 'a second time'.
4
Examine the second proof from the Quran
Consider verse 36:31 which states that destroyed generations do not return to the living, implying no return before Judgment Day.
5
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet's statement that after death there is only Paradise or Hellfire precludes any worldly return.

A section on refuting the extremists of the Shi'a who say that Imam Ali (peace be upon him) will return. A group of the Rawafid said: Indeed Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) and his companions will return to this world and will take revenge from their enemies and will fill the earth with justice just as it had been filled with tyranny and oppression. [Ya-Sin 31]; and likewise his saying (peace be upon him): 'There is nothing after death except Paradise and the Fire.'

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a specific Shi'a extremist belief. The author first presents the claim of the Rawafid: that Imam Ali and his companions will return to this world before the Day of Judgment to exact revenge and establish justice, filling the earth with fairness as it had been filled with tyranny. Then he states the Sunni position: anyone who dies does not return to this world until the Day of Resurrection, because there is no evidence supporting such a return. He then provides three proofs: 1) The Quranic verse from Surah Ta-Ha (20:55) which says 'from it (the earth) We created you, and into it We shall return you, and from it We shall bring you out another time.' The author notes that Allah said 'another time' (tāratan ukhrā) and not 'a second time,' indicating only one return at resurrection. 2) The verse from Surah Ya-Sin (36:31) which asks whether the disbelievers do not see how many generations were destroyed and that they (the destroyed ones) will not return to them (the living), implying no return before Judgment Day. 3) The hadith of the Prophet: 'There is nothing after death except Paradise and the Fire,' meaning the soul goes directly to the afterlife, not back to this world.

الرجعة (al-raj'a)
غلاة الشيعة (ghulat al-shi'a)
الروافض (al-rawafid)
أهل السنة والجماعة (ahl al-sunna wa al-jama'a)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the dead can return to this world before the final resurrection, as believed by certain Shi'a groups.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna hold that no one returns to this world after death; the soul goes to the afterlife and awaits resurrection.

B) They do not return until the Day of Resurrection
C) Only prophets return
D) They return in a different form

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position is that death finalizes one's worldly life, and no one returns until the Day of Resurrection; this is supported by Quran and hadith.

Refutation of the Permissive Sect on Prohibited Acts
Refutes the permissive sect that declares forbidden acts permissible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the permissive sect's fallacious arguments for declaring forbidden acts permissible and the Sunni refutation based on hadith.

Core Idea
No act becomes permissible just by calling it something else or misinterpreting Quran.

This lesson examines a group that attempted to justify wine, sodomy, and entertainment by misusing Quranic verses and attributing their views to Imam Malik. The Sunni scholars respond with a clear prophetic hadith that restricts permissible play to three specific activities. Understanding this refutation helps you recognize how deviant groups manipulate scripture.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the permissive claims
Find the claims that wine is 'not forbidden but disliked', sodomy is 'halal', and dancing/singing/poetry are 'halal'. Notice the Quranic verses they cite.
2
Understand the misuse of Quran
The permissive group cites Quran 5:93 to excuse wine and Quran 29:29 to argue that sodomy is not forbidden. Recognize that these verses are either abrogated or taken out of context.
3
Learn the Sunni counter-evidence
The people of Sunna use the Prophet's hadith that all play is forbidden except three specified ones. This refutes the permissive claims comprehensively.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how the misuse of scripture by deviant groups can be countered by authentic hadith and proper Quranic interpretation.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
[ في الرد على الإباحية ]
وصِنْفٌ من الشّيعة قالوا بأن الخمر ليس بحرام، لكنه مكروه. قال الله تعالى: ﴿لَيْسَ عَلَى الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ جُنَاحٌ فِيمَا طَعِمُوا إِذَا مَا اتَّقَوْا وَآمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ ثُمَّ اتَّقَوْا وَآمَنُوا ثُمَّ اتَّقَوْا وَأَحْسَنُوا وَاللهُ يُحِبُّ الْمُحْسِنِينَ﴾ [المائدة: ٩٣] وكذلك قالوا: بأن اللُّواطة حلال؛ لأن الله سماها منكرًا ولم تحرم في كتابه نصاً. قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَتَأْتُونَ فِي نَادِيكُمُ الْمُنكَرَ﴾ [العنكبوت: ٢٩] .
وكذلك الرقص والغناء والشعر حلال. وقالوا: هذا قول مالك بن أنس رضي الله عنه إمام المدينة.
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة : كلُّ ذلك حرام لقوله عليه السلام: «كل لعب [ولهو ](٢) حرام إلا ثلاث رمية من قوسه، وتأديب فرسه وملاعبة الرجل مع أهله» وقال الله
A section [on refuting the permissive sect]. A group of the Shi'a said that wine is not forbidden, but disliked. Allah the Most High said: 'There is no sin upon those who believe and do righteous deeds concerning what they have eaten [in the past] if they fear Allah, believe, and do righteous deeds, then fear Allah and believe, then fear Allah and do good; and Allah loves the good-doers' [al-Ma'ida 93]. And likewise they said that sodomy is lawful because Allah called it an abomination and did not forbid it explicitly in His Book. Allah the Most High said: 'And you commit the abomination in your assemblies' [al-Ankabut 29]. And likewise dancing, singing, and poetry are lawful. And they said: this is the statement of Malik ibn Anas (may Allah be pleased with him), the Imam of Medina. And the people of the Sunna and the Jama'a said: All of that is forbidden because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'Every play [and amusement] is forbidden except three: shooting one's bow, training one's horse, and a man playing with his wife.' And Allah said...
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the permissive sect (al-Ibāḥiyya) that makes forbidden things permissible. The author first presents their claims: 1) Wine is not haram but only makruh (disliked). They cite Quran 5:93, which absolves those who believed and did good deeds from blame concerning what they consumed in the past, but the author shows this verse is abrogated or specific to early Muslims before the prohibition. 2) They claim sodomy (liwāṭ) is halal because Allah called it 'munkar' (abomination) but did not explicitly forbid it in the Quran. They cite Quran 29:29. 3) They claim dancing, singing, and poetry are halal. They attribute this view to Imam Malik, the Imam of Medina. Then the author states the Sunni position: everything mentioned is haram, based on the Prophet's hadith: 'Every play [and amusement] is forbidden except three: shooting one's bow, training one's horse, and a man playing with his wife.' The passage ends abruptly with 'And Allah said...' suggesting further Quranic proof is implied. The commentary notes that the Shi'a cited verses out of context and ignored clear prohibitions.

Key Terms
الإباحية (al-ibāḥiyya)
الخمر (al-khamr)
اللواطة (al-liwāṭa)
الرقص (al-raqṣ)
الغناء (al-ghinā')
الشعر (al-shi'r)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that calling an act 'munkar' (abomination) implies it is not forbidden.
Correction: In Islamic law, 'munkar' is something that is prohibited; it does not indicate permissibility.

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, what is the ruling on the acts mentioned (wine, sodomy, dancing, singing, poetry)?
A) All are permissible
B) All are forbidden
C) Only wine is forbidden
D) Only sodomy is forbidden

Key Takeaway
The permissive sect's claims are refuted by the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that forbids all play except three specified activities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself reinterpreting a clear command of Allah to justify a desire? What verse or hadith have you twisted, and how will you repent and align with the truth today?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) specified only three permissible forms of play. Which of your own leisure activities would you honestly measure against this hadith, and what change must you make?
?
When you hear someone claim that a sin is permissible based on a misquoted verse, do you have the courage to challenge them with the Sunnah, or do you stay silent? Commit now to learning one hadith to defend the truth.

Refutation of Mut'ah Marriage: The Sunni Position
Imam Nasafi refutes the Rawafid claim that mut'ah marriage is permissible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Sunni position that mut'ah (temporary marriage) is forbidden is proven through abrogation of the verses cited by the Rawafid.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is forbidden like wine, abrogated by the same Quran.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi directly engages a sectarian claim by the Rawafid that mut'ah marriage is permissible. He presents their proof from the Quran and then refutes it by citing abrogation and the punishment for zina. This lesson walks through the argument step by step, showing how the Sunni position is firmly grounded in scripture.

Guided Path
1
Read the Rawafid claim
Read the Rawafid's statement that mut'ah is halal and their proof from Quran 4:24. Notice how they interpret the verse to mean payment for mere enjoyment without a permanent marriage.
2
Understand the Sunni ruling
The author states that mut'ah is forbidden like wine. Note the strong analogy — it is not just disliked but strictly prohibited.
3
Identify the first abrogation
The Sunni proof uses Quran 24:2 (zina punishment) to show that mut'ah, being time-limited intercourse, falls under zina and therefore abrogates any earlier permission.
The verse of flogging applies to both parties of zina.
4
See the second abrogation
The verse the Rawafid cite (4:24) is also abrogated by later marriage commands (4:2 and 24:32). This shows that even if 4:24 originally permitted something, it was replaced by permanent marriage.
These verses command marriage of what is pleasant and marrying the unmarried.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الرد على من قال بإباحة زواج المتعة وصنف من الروافض قالوا بأن المتعة حلال، وهو استئجار المرأة للوطء. قال الله تعالى: (فَمَا اسْتَمْتَعْتُم بِهِ مِنْهُنَّ فَكَاتُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ فَرِيضَةً) [النساء: ٢٤] أوجب الأجرة بمجرد الاستمتاع دون النكاح.
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة المتعة حرام كالخمر، إلا أنها أبيحت في سَفَرٍ واحد للضرورة ثم نُسِخَتْ بقوله تعالى: ﴿ الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي فَاجْلِدُوا كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مِائَةَ جَلْدَةٍ وَلَا تَأْخُذَكُر بيهما رأْفَةٌ فِي دِينِ اللَّهِ إِن كُنتُمْ تُؤْمِنُونَ بِاللَّهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ وَلْيَشْهَدْ عَذَابَهُمَا طَائِفَةٌ مِّنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ ﴾ [النور: ٢]. وأما الآية قلنا: الآية نُسِخَتْ بقوله تعالى: [ فَانكِحُوا مَا طَابَ لَكُم مِّنَ النِّسَاءِ ) [النساء: (٢) وَأَنكِحُوا الْأَيْمَى مِنكُمْ﴾ [النور: ٣٢].
Chapter on refuting those who said that the permissibility of mut'ah marriage. A group of the Rawafid said that mut'ah is lawful, and it is hiring a woman for intercourse. Allah Almighty said: (So for whatever you have enjoyed from them, give them their due compensation as an obligation) [An-Nisa: 24] – He made the payment obligatory merely for enjoyment without marriage. And Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah said: mut'ah is forbidden like wine, except that it was permitted in one journey out of necessity, then it was abrogated by His statement: (The fornicatress and the fornicator, flog each one of them with one hundred lashes, and let not pity for them seize you in the religion of Allah, if you believe in Allah and the Last Day, and let a group of the believers witness their punishment) [An-Nur: 2]. As for the [first] verse, we said: the verse was abrogated by His statement: (Then marry what is pleasant to you of women) [An-Nisa: 2] and (And marry the unmarried among you) [An-Nur: 32].
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Rawafid (a Shi'a group) who claim that mut'ah (temporary marriage) is lawful. The author first states the Rawafid position: mut'ah is halal, defined as hiring a woman for intercourse. They cite Quran 4:24 – 'so for whatever you have enjoyed from them, give them their due compensation' – arguing that the verse obligates payment for mere enjoyment without a permanent marriage contract. The author then presents the Sunni position: mut'ah is haram (forbidden) like wine. It was temporarily permitted once during a specific journey due to necessity, but later abrogated. The proof of abrogation is Quran 24:2, the verse on flogging for zina (illicit sexual intercourse). Since mut'ah involves a sexual relationship with a time limit, it is a form of zina and thus subject to the punishment. Furthermore, the verse the Rawafid cite (4:24) is itself abrogated by later verses that command marriage: 4:2 'marry what is pleasant to you of women' in the context of permanent marriage, and 24:32 'marry the unmarried among you'. These verses replace the temporary permission with the institution of proper, permanent marriage.

Key Terms
متعة
روافض
أهل السنة والجماعة
نسخ
استمتاع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Quran 4:24 unconditionally permits mut'ah marriage without any restrictions.
Correction: The verse was abrogated by later verses (4:2, 24:32) and the zina punishment verse (24:2), so it no longer applies.

Checkpoint
What is the status of mut'ah marriage according to Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah in this passage?
A) It is permissible like any other marriage.
B) It is forbidden like wine, and was abrogated.
C) It is recommended during travel.
D) It is merely disliked but not haram.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position that mut'ah is haram is established by the abrogation of its temporary permission through the zina punishment verse and the definitive commands for permanent marriage.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there any areas of your life where you justify sin by calling it something else, as the Rawafid call mut'ah a marriage? What would it take for you to accept Allah's command as final, even when it contradicts your desires?
?
The companions had to leave behind a temporary pleasure because Allah abrogated it. What temporary pleasures are you holding onto that Allah has clearly forbidden? Will you submit even if it feels like a loss?
?
If you truly believed that every abrogation from Allah is for your protection, how would your relationship with forbidden desires change starting today?

Refutation of Claim that Love Abolishes Religious Duties
Refutation of the claim that extreme love removes outward worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why extreme love does not nullify outward worship and how the examples of prophets refute this claim.

Core Idea
Love does not cancel worship; prophets perfected love yet worshipped.

This lesson addresses a dangerous misconception: that extreme love for Allah can make one independent of Sharia obligations. A group called Ahl al-Ibaha claimed that at the peak of love, outward worship falls away and is replaced by mere contemplation, and that such a person ascends bodily to heaven. The Ahl al-Sunnah refutes this by pointing to the prophets themselves, who were the most beloved yet still performed worship and never ascended except by Allah's command. Let's examine the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the claim of Ahl al-Ibaha
Read the first part of the Arabic passage describing their belief. Notice the specific acts they claim are dropped (prayer, zakat, hajj) and what replaces them (contemplation).
2
Understand the refutation using prophetic examples
The Ahl al-Sunnah's refutation uses four Quranic verses showing that prophets did not ascend by themselves. Identify each prophet and the verse cited.
The refutation concludes that if prophets did not ascend, others certainly cannot.
3
Reflect on the logical conclusion
Ask yourself: why is the belief of Ahl al-Ibaha considered disbelief? The answer lies in their denial of the obligations that even prophets fulfilled.
This shows that love does not exempt from Sharia; rather, love motivates obedience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أهل الإباحة: إذا بلغ العبد في الحب غاية المحبة تسقط عنه العبادة الظاهرة نحو الصَّلاة والزَّكاة والحج وغير ذلك، وكانت عبادته بعد ذلك التفكر، ويصعد بنوره إلى السماء، ويدخل الجنة ويعانق الحور العين ويدخل القصور ويباضعهن. وقال أهل السنة والجماعة من اعتقد هذا يكفر؛ لأن الأنبياء عليهم السلام لم يصعدوا بأنفسهم إلى السماء كما قال الله تعالى في حق نبينا محمد: سُبْحَانَ الَّذِي أَسْرَى بِعَبْدِهِ لَيْلًا ﴾ [الإسراء: ١] الآية، وفي حق عيسى عليه السلام: بَل رَفَعَهُ اللهُ إِلَيْهِ ) [النساء: ١٥٨] وفي حق آدم عليه السلام: اسْكُنْ أَنتَ وَزَوْجُكَ الْجَنَّةَ ) [البقرة: ٣٥] وفي حق إدريس عليه السلام: وَرَفَعْتَهُ مَكَانًا عَلِيًّا ﴾ [مريم: ٥٧] فغيرهم أولى أن لا يصعدوا.
The people of al-Ibaha said: When the servant reaches in love the extreme of love, outward worship such as prayer, zakat, pilgrimage, and others falls away from him, and his worship after that is contemplation, and he ascends with his light to heaven, enters paradise, embraces the houris, enters palaces, and has intercourse with them. And the people of the Sunnah and the community said: Whoever believes this disbelieves, because the prophets, peace be upon them, did not ascend by themselves to heaven, as Allah Almighty said concerning our Prophet Muhammad: 'Exalted is He who took His servant by night' [al-Isra: 1] the verse, and concerning Jesus, peace be upon him: 'Rather, Allah raised him to Himself' [an-Nisa: 158], and concerning Adam, peace be upon him: 'Dwell, you and your wife, in Paradise' [al-Baqara: 35], and concerning Idris, peace be upon him: 'And We raised him to a high station' [Maryam: 57]. So others are more deserving not to ascend.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage presents a deviant claim and its refutation. The first part is the claim of a group called 'Ahl al-Ibaha' (those who permit licentiousness). They assert that when a believer reaches the ultimate level of love for God, all obligatory outward acts of worship (like prayer, zakat, hajj) are no longer required. Instead, their worship becomes mere contemplation (tafakkur). They also believe that such a person can ascend bodily (with his light) to heaven, enjoy paradise, and have physical relations with the houris. The refutation from Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah is decisive: anyone who holds this belief is a disbeliever (kafir). The proof is that even the prophets—who are the highest in love and station—did not ascend to heaven by their own power or will. The author cites four examples: Prophet Muhammad was taken by night (Isra) by divine command, Jesus was raised (raf') by Allah, Adam was placed in Paradise by Allah's command, and Idris was raised to a high place. All these ascents were acts of Allah, not self-initiated. Since the prophets themselves did not ascend on their own, it is even more impossible for anyone else to do so. Thus, the claim of al-Ibaha is false and constitutes disbelief.

Key Terms
أهل الإباحة
سقوط التكاليف
التفكر
العبادة الظاهرة
أهل السنة والجماعة
تكفير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that extreme love for Allah means one is no longer required to perform outward acts of worship like prayer and fasting.
Correction: The passage shows that even the prophets, who had the most perfect love, still performed worship and did not ascend except by Allah's command.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main evidence against the claim of Ahl al-Ibaha?
A) The prophets never experienced extreme love.
B) The prophets did not ascend to heaven by themselves.
C) The prophets forbade contemplation.
D) The prophets were perfect in love yet still performed outward worship.

Key Takeaway
The claim that love abolishes worship is false; even prophets observed obligations and only ascended by Allah's will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that your love for Allah is so deep that you can skip prayers or other obligations without guilt? What does this lesson force you to reconsider about that feeling?
?
The prophets, who loved Allah more than anyone, still prayed, fasted, and gave charity. What excuse have you been using to neglect any act of worship, and how will you remove that excuse starting today?
?
If you believe that mere contemplation or spiritual feelings can replace physical worship, where has that belief led you in your daily life? Will you now repent from that and commit to the outward duties that the prophets themselves performed?

The Deviant Claim of Permissibility of Taking Others' Wealth and Women
Exposition of the deviant claim on property and women.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand a deviant theological claim that permits taking others' property and women based on need, and its flawed justification.

Core Idea
Need is not a license to violate property and marital rights.

In this lesson, we encounter a radical claim attributed to some deviant groups: that all property and women are intrinsically permissible, and that need gives one the right to take what belongs to another. The passage presents their reasoning, which appeals to the common inheritance from Adam and Eve. Understanding this claim helps us recognize the boundaries that Islamic law places on ownership and marital rights.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the two elements of the claim: permissibility of property and permissibility of women.
The passage does not include the refutation; we are only exposed to the deviant view.
2
Identify the core of the claim
The proponents say that wealth and women are created by Allah and thus inherently permissible (mubah) among people. Need justifies taking them.
3
Examine the justification
They argue that since Adam and Eve died, their wealth is equally shared among all humans. This is a flawed analogy meant to abolish private ownership and marital bonds.
Consider why this reasoning is invalid from an Islamic perspective.
4
Reflect on the implications
If this claim were accepted, it would lead to anarchy and violation of clear Islamic rulings on property and marriage. This highlights the importance of divine legislation.
The refutation, though absent here, would likely cite texts on ownership and marital rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من قال: إن الله تعالى خلق النساء والمال وذلك مباح فيما بينهم، حتى إن من احتاج إلى مال غيره فله أن يأخذه، وكذلك إذا احتاج إلى نِسْوة غيره فله أن يأخذها، لأن آدم وحواء عليهما السلام ماتا وبقي مالهما بيننا على السواء.
And among them are those who said: Indeed Allah created women and property, and that is permissible among them, such that if one needs the property of another, he may take it, and likewise if he needs the women of another, he may take them, because Adam and Eve, peace be upon them, died and their wealth remained among us equally.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage presents another deviant view, likely from the same group (Ahl al-Ibaha) or a related sect. They make two claims: (1) Since Allah created women and wealth, they are intrinsically permissible (mubah) for everyone; (2) Therefore, if a person needs someone else's property or women (wives), he is allowed to take them. Their justification is that Adam and Eve died, and their property (the entire earth?) is common among all humans equally. This reasoning implies that private ownership and marital rights are invalid, leading to complete anarchy. The author does not provide a refutation within this page, but the context of the chapter (Refutation of those who claim the falling away of religious obligations) suggests that this view is also considered false and disbelief. The absence of a refutation here may be because the author expects the reader to understand the sheer absurdity of the claim, or the refutation follows in subsequent pages.

Key Terms
إباحة النساء والمال
آدم وحواء
السواء
الاحتياج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Need makes other people's property and women permissible to take.
Correction: Islamic law prohibits taking others' property or women without consent, regardless of need, unless through legitimate means (e.g., charity, lawful marriage).

Checkpoint
What justification do the proponents give for taking others' property and women?
A) The prophets allowed it.
B) Adam and Eve died and left their wealth to all humans equally.
C) Allah created everything for everyone.
D) The rich must share with the poor.

Key Takeaway
The claim that need justifies taking others' property and women is a deviant view based on a flawed understanding of Adam and Eve's inheritance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever justified taking something that wasn't yours by telling yourself you needed it more than the owner? What does this lesson reveal about the danger of such thinking?
?
Do you treat the boundaries Allah has set around others' property and family as absolute, or do you sometimes feel above them? Ask yourself: where is your heart right now?
?
If you saw a fellow Muslim in need, would your first instinct be to help them lawfully or to take from them? What does your answer say about your understanding of justice?

Refuting the Claim that Worship Falls Away for the Lovers of Allah
Refutation of the Ibahiyya claim using prophetic examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ahl al-Sunna reject the claim that extreme love for Allah removes the obligation of external worship, using the examples of the prophets.

Core Idea
Even the prophets, the greatest lovers of Allah, never abandoned worship.

The claim that when a person reaches the ultimate stage of love for Allah, all outward acts of worship fall away from him is an extreme and false notion. This lesson examines the reasoning of those who hold this view, known as the Ibahiyya, and the decisive refutation provided by Ahl al-Sunna based on the lives of the prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the claim of the Ibahiyya
Read the first part of the passage where the people of Ibahah describe what happens when a servant attains extreme love: worship falls away, replaced by contemplation, and he ascends to paradise etc.
Notice how they claim a direct entrance to paradise without the usual means.
2
Understand the refutation
Read the response of Ahl al-Sunna: whoever believes this disbelieves, because the prophets did not ascend by themselves.
The key is the prophets are the beloved of Allah, yet they did not skip worship.
3
Examine the prophetic examples
Look at the four Quranic verses cited about Prophet Muhammad, Jesus, Adam, and Idris. They show that even these great prophets were taken by Allah, not by their own power, and they never claimed a drop in worship.
The argument is from the greater to the lesser: if prophets didn't, others are more deserving not to.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes by affirming that such a belief is kufr. Reflect on why Ahl al-Sunna considered it so serious.
This shows the importance of adhering to Sharia regardless of spiritual station.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الرد على من قال بسقوط التكاليف الشرعية
قال أهل الإباحة: إذا بلغ العبد في الحب غاية المحبة تسقط عنه العبادة الظاهرة نحو الصلاة والزكاة والحج وغير ذلك، وكانت عبادته بعد ذلك التفكر، ويصعد بنوره إلى السماء، ويدخل الجنة ويعانق الحور العين ويدخل القصور ويباضعهن.
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة من اعتقد هذا يكفر؛ لأن الأنبياء عليهم السلام لم يصعدوا بأنفسهم إلى السماء كما قال الله تعالى في حق نبينا محمد: سبحان الذي أسرى بعبده ليلا الآية، وفي حق عيسى عليه السلام: بل رفعه الله إليه، وفي حق آدم عليه السلام: اسكن أنت وزوجك الجنة، وفي حق إدريس عليه السلام: ورفعناه مكانا عليا، فغيرهم أولى أن لا يصعدوا.
Chapter on refuting those who say that the legal obligations fall away. The people of Ibahah said: When a servant reaches the extreme of love in love, outward worship such as prayer, zakat, hajj and other than that falls away from him, and his worship after that is contemplation, and he ascends with his light to the sky, enters Paradise, embraces the houris, enters palaces, and cohabits with them. The people of the Sunnah and the community said: Whoever believes this disbelieves, because the prophets, peace be upon them, did not ascend by themselves to the sky, as Allah said regarding our Prophet Muhammad: 'Exalted is He who took His servant by night' (al-Isra 17:1) the verse, and regarding Jesus, peace be upon him: 'Rather, Allah raised him to Himself' (an-Nisa 4:158), and regarding Adam, peace be upon him: 'Dwell, you and your wife, in Paradise' (al-Baqara 2:35), and regarding Idris, peace be upon him: 'And We raised him to a high station' (Maryam 19:57). So others are more deserving not to ascend.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a deviant claim. It begins by stating the chapter's purpose: to refute those who say the legal obligations fall away. Then it presents the claim of the Ibahiyya (those who permit such things): they assert that when a person reaches the ultimate stage of love for God, all external acts of worship (like prayer, zakat, hajj) are lifted from him; his only worship becomes contemplation; he ascends in spirit to heaven, enters Paradise, embraces the houris, enters palaces, and has sexual relations with them. In response, the Ahl al-Sunna declare that anyone who holds this belief is a disbeliever. The reason is that the prophets—the most beloved of Allah—did not ascend by their own power or without divine command. The author cites four proofs: The Prophet Muhammad was taken on the Night Journey by Allah, not by himself; Jesus was raised to Allah; Adam was placed in Paradise by Allah; Idris was raised to a high station. If even these great prophets did not ascend on their own, certainly those who claim such for themselves are false. Thus the argument uses prophetic precedent to invalidate the Ibahi claim.

Key Terms
سقوط التكاليف الشرعية
أهل الإباحة
أهل السنة والجماعة
العبادة الظاهرة
التفكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: When a person reaches extreme love for Allah, all external acts of worship (prayer, zakat, hajj) fall away from him, and he can ascend to paradise by his own light.
Correction: The prophets, who are the ultimate lovers of Allah, never stopped worshiping and never ascended by their own power; they were taken by Allah. Therefore, no one can claim that love removes obligations.

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason Ahl al-Sunna deem those who believe obligations fall away as disbelievers?
A) Because such a belief leads to abandoning prayer
B) Because the prophets did not ascend by themselves nor drop worship
C) Because the Ibahiyya are a known heretical sect
D) Because the Quran explicitly states obligations never fall away

Key Takeaway
True love for Allah does not cancel the obligations of worship; rather, the prophets demonstrated the perfect balance of love and devotion through their steadfast adherence to Sharia.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that your love for Allah is so deep that some acts of worship seem unnecessary or burdensome? How does the example of the prophets, who loved Allah most, challenge that feeling? What will you change in your attitude toward obligatory worship today?
?
The Ibahis believed that contemplation (tafakkur) could replace prayer. In what ways might you be subtly substituting 'spiritual' experiences—like listening to lectures, feeling emotional, or having deep thoughts—for the actual commanded acts of worship? Will you recommit to outward obedience even when your inner state feels high?
?
Read the Quranic verses cited about the prophets' ascents: each was by Allah's direct command, not by their own striving. What does this teach you about your attempts to 'reach' Allah through your own methods or spiritual experiences? Are you willing to submit to Allah's path as shown by the prophets, rather than inventing your own? What is one specific worship you will do today purely because Allah commanded it, not because you feel like it?

Property and Women are Not Common Property
Refutes the claim that others' property and women are permissible to take freely.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that property and women are common is false, and how the Ahl al-Sunna respond using the Quran and Hadith.

Core Idea
No one may take another's wealth or women without their willing consent.

Some groups argued that since all humans descend from Adam, all property and women are common and can be taken freely. The Ahl al-Sunna firmly reject this, grounding their position in clear Quranic verse and prophetic hadith. In this lesson, we examine that deviant claim and the orthodox response.

Guided Path
1
Read the deviant claim
First, read the passage describing the heretical view: that Allah created women and property as common, so anyone in need can take them. Note the rationale involving Adam and Eve.
This view is attributed to some deviant sect, not mainstream Islam.
2
Study the Sunni response
Then read the Ahl al-Sunna's reply: property is only lawful with the owner's good pleasure. They quote the Quranic verse forbidding consuming wealth unjustly and allowing only trade by mutual consent.
3
Examine the Hadith evidence
The passage also cites the well-known hadith: 'The burden of proof is on the claimant, and the oath is on the one who denies.' Understand how this hadith supports the inviolability of property.
This hadith places the responsibility on the one making a claim, not on the owner to prove ownership.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how this refutation upholds the sanctity of individual rights in Islam, especially regarding wealth and family.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من قال: إن الله تعالى خلق النساء والمال وذلك مباح فيما بينهم، حتى إن من احتاج إلى مال غيره فله أن يأخذه، وكذلك إذا احتاج إلى نسوة غيره فله أن يأخذها، لأن آدم وحواء عليهما السلام ماتا وبقي مالهما بيننا على السواء.
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: لا يحل مال امرئ مسلم إلا بطيبة من نفسه. قال الله تعالى: يا أيها الذين آمنوا لا تأكلوا أموالكم بينكم بالباطل إلا أن تكون تجارة عن تراض منكم والأحاديث الواردة في هذا الباب كثيرة منها قوله عليه السلام: البينة على المدعي واليمين على من أنكر.
And among them are those who said: Indeed Allah created women and property, and that is permissible among them, so that whoever needs the property of another may take it, and likewise if he needs the women of another he may take them, because Adam and Eve, peace be upon them, died and their property remained among us equally. The people of the Sunnah and the community said: The property of a Muslim man is not lawful except with his good pleasure. Allah said: 'O you who have believed, do not consume one another's wealth unjustly, but only [in lawful] business by mutual consent' (an-Nisa 4:29). And the traditions narrated in this chapter are many, among them his saying, peace be upon him: 'The burden of proof is on the claimant, and the oath is on the one who denies.'
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a second claim. The author presents the heretical view: some assert that Allah created women and property as common for all, so anyone who needs someone else's money or women may simply take them, claiming that all property descends equally from Adam and Eve. The Ahl al-Sunna response is unequivocal: a Muslim's property is not lawful except with his willing consent. They support this with the Quranic verse forbidding consuming wealth unjustly and allowing only trade by mutual agreement. Then they cite the famous hadith that the burden of proof is on the claimant, meaning that one cannot simply take another's property without evidence or permission. Thus the claim of common ownership based on Adam's legacy is invalid under Islamic law.

Key Terms
إباحة المال والنساء
بطيبة من نفسه
تجارة عن تراض
البينة على المدعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because all humans descend from Adam, all property and women are common and can be taken freely.
Correction: Islam upholds individual ownership; property is inviolable without the owner's willing consent, as per Quran and Hadith.

Checkpoint
What is the main evidence Ahl al-Sunna use to reject the claim that others' wealth can be freely taken?
A) The story of Adam and Eve
B) The verse about consuming wealth unjustly and the hadith on proof
C) The consensus of scholars
D) The fact that people would object

Key Takeaway
Islam strictly prohibits taking another person's property or women without their willing consent, as established by the Quran and the Prophet's hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The deviant claim in this lesson used Adam and Eve as an excuse to take what is not theirs. Think of one area in your life—a relationship, a responsibility, or a possession—where you have rationalized a wrong action by some twisted reasoning. What specific verse or hadith from this lesson will you use to correct your thinking today?
?
The hadith says 'The burden of proof is on the claimant.' In your daily interactions, do you ever assume you are owed something—attention, respect, or material goods—without having a rightful claim? How would this hadith change your behavior in the next 24 hours?
?
You have read that a Muslim's property is not lawful except with his willing consent. Is there anything you own that was obtained without the full, willing consent of the previous owner? What step will you take to make it right, even if it is uncomfortable?

Refutation of Permitting Others' Wives and Slave Girls
Refutes the claim that others' women become permissible at extreme love.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic position that sexual relations are only lawful through marriage or ownership, and that extreme love does not override divine law.

Core Idea
Extreme love does not make the unlawful lawful.

This passage addresses a dangerous claim: that a person who reaches extreme love for Allah can take others' wives and slave-girls as if they were flowers. The Sunni response is firm: only marriage and ownership make women lawful. The Quran and the case of Ma'iz provide clear evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the deviant claim
Read the first part of the passage where a group claims that extreme love makes others' women lawful like flowers.
Notice they use the phrase 'حبيب الله' to justify this.
2
Read the Sunni response
Read the response from Ahl al-Sunna: women are only lawful through marriage (nikah) and slave-girls through ownership (milk).
They also mention the case of a married slave-girl.
3
Identify the two proofs
Find the Quranic verse (an-Nur 24:2) and the story of Ma'iz that are cited as evidence.
These prove that illicit relations are punishable, so they cannot be lawful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من قال: إذا بلغ العبد في الحب غاية المحبة تحل له نساء الغير وإماء الغير، فهن كالرياحين له أن يشمهن لأن هذا حبيب الله والنساء إماء الله، والحبيب لا يمنع حبيبه عما يريد.
وقال المسلمون وهم أهل السنة والجماعة: لا تحل النساء إلا بالنكاح، والإماء إلا بالملك وبالنكاح أيضًا إذا زوجها المولى من غيره تحل له وهى أمته يدل عليه قال الله تعالى: الزانية والزاني فاجلدوا كل واحد منهما مائة جلدة ولأن ماعزا زنى فرجم، فلو كان حلالا لما استحق الرجم.
And among them are those who said: When the servant reaches the extreme of love in love, the women of others and the slave-girls of others become lawful for him, for they are like fragrant flowers for him to smell, because this one is the beloved of Allah, and women are bondwomen of Allah, and the beloved does not prevent his beloved from what he desires. The Muslims, who are the people of the Sunnah and the community, said: Women are not lawful except through marriage, and slave-girls except through ownership, and also through marriage if the master marries her off to someone else, she becomes lawful to him while she is his slave-girl. This is indicated by Allah's statement: 'The female and male fornicator, flog each one of them with one hundred lashes' (an-Nur 24:2), and because Ma'iz committed adultery and was stoned; if it had been lawful, he would not have deserved stoning.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage refutes a third claim. The deviant view is that a person who reaches extreme love may have any other's wife or slave-girl, likening them to flowers. The Ahl al-Sunna counter by declaring that women are only lawful through marriage (nikah) and slave-girls through ownership (milk); additionally, a married slave-girl is lawful to her husband. They provide two proofs: first, the Quranic verse prescribing flogging for fornicators, which indicates that illicit relations are prohibited. Second, the case of Ma'iz who committed adultery and was stoned by order of the Prophet; if it had been lawful, he would not have been punished. Thus, the deviant claim that love permits such actions is false.

Key Terms
نساء الغير
إماء الغير
النكاح
الملك
الرياحين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: When a servant reaches extreme love for Allah, others' women become permissible for him.
Correction: Only marriage (nikah) or ownership (milk) make women lawful; the Quran and Sunnah punish zina, showing it is never permissible.

Checkpoint
What evidence does the passage give against the claim that others' women are permissible at extreme love?
A) The hadith about burden of proof
B) The Quranic verse on zina and the stoning of Ma'iz
C) The story of Adam and Eve
D) The consensus of the companions

Key Takeaway
Extreme love for Allah does not permit violating His prohibitions; sexual relations are only lawful through marriage or ownership.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that your spiritual rank or closeness to Allah excuses you from following a difficult command? This lesson says no. What command have you been ignoring because you assumed your love for Allah made it unnecessary?
?
The deviant view compared others' women to flowers to be enjoyed. In what ways do you objectify people to satisfy your desires while still considering yourself a believer? How can you change this?
?
Ma'iz was stoned despite being a Muslim. Do you truly believe you will be held accountable for every hidden sin, or do you rely on feeling spiritual to avoid consequences? What does your answer reveal about your heart?

Refuting the Claim of Immunity from Fire for Sinners
Refutes the claim that extreme love exempts from Hell for major sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the belief that extreme lovers of God are immune from Hellfire for major sins is rejected as a false doctrine.

Core Idea
No one is immune from Hellfire based on love alone; actions matter.

This lesson examines a deviant claim that those who reach extreme love for Allah are exempt from punishment for major sins. The passage dismisses it as false doctrine, reminding us that no spiritual rank overrides divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the author's words. Then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: claim followed by rejection.
The passage is short, so focus on the key terms.
2
Identify the claim and its reasoning
The deviant group argues that extreme love prevents entry into Hell, even for major sins, because Hell is permanent just as Paradise is permanent. Find this logic.
They use a false analogy between the permanence of Paradise and Hell.
3
Understand why it is rejected
The author ends by saying 'This is their false doctrine.' Reflect on why this contradicts core Sunni beliefs about divine justice and the role of repentance and punishment.
This claim undermines the seriousness of sin and the possibility of temporary punishment or forgiveness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من قال: إذا بلغ العبد في الحب غاية المحبة إذا ارتكب الكبيرة لا يدخله الله تعالى النار، لأن كل من دخل النار لا يخرج كداخل الجنة، وهذا مذهبهم الباطل.
And among them are those who said: When the servant reaches the extreme of love in love, if he commits a major sin, Allah will not make him enter the Fire, because everyone who enters the Fire does not come out, like the one who enters Paradise. This is their false doctrine.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a short refutation of a fourth claim. The author attributes to the deviant group the belief that when a person reaches extreme love for God, even if he commits a kabira (major sin), Allah will not send him to Hell. They argue that anyone who enters Hell never leaves, analogous to how one who enters Paradise never leaves (i.e., it is a permanent state). The author concludes dismissively: 'This is their false doctrine' (madhhabuhum al-batil). The brevity implies that such a claim contradicts clear Quranic threats of punishment for sin and the consensus of Ahl al-Sunna that sinners among believers may enter the Fire temporarily or be forgiven, but no one is immune.

Key Terms
الكبيرة
النار
الجنة
مذهبهم الباطل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the passage characterize the belief that extreme lovers are immune from Hellfire for major sins?
A) As a valid opinion among scholars
B) As a false doctrine (مذهبهم الباطل)
C) As a topic of debate
D) As accepted by some Ahl al-Sunna

Key Takeaway
The belief that extreme love exempts from divine punishment is a false doctrine rejected by Ahl al-Sunna.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself thinking that because you 'love Allah' you can let certain sins slide without consequence? How does this passage's blunt verdict of 'false doctrine' confront that comfortable assumption? What will you change today in response?
?

?
Ask yourself: Do I rely on my spiritual feelings as a shield against accountability? The source says no one is immune based on love alone. What sin in your life have you been excusing as 'okay' because you feel close to Allah? How will you use this lesson to break that illusion?
