Refuting the Claim that Extreme Love Permits Others' Women
Imam Nasafi refutes a deviant claim that extreme love makes others' women lawful, citing Islamic law.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi refutes the extremist claim that extreme love makes others' women lawful, using Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Extreme spiritual love does not override the Shari'ah; lawful relations require marriage or ownership.

This lesson presents a dangerous antinomian claim that has appeared in Muslim history: that those who reach the highest level of love for Allah are permitted to have any woman they desire. Imam Nasafi refutes this by citing clear Quranic evidence and the example of the Prophet's ruling on adultery.

Guided Path
1
Identify the deviant claim
Read the passage and note the claim that when a person reaches extreme love, others' women become lawful like flowers to smell. Understand the flawed reasoning behind it.
The claim is based on a false analogy: the 'beloved of Allah' should not be denied anything.
2
Learn the Sunni response
Imam Nasafi and Ahl al-Sunnah state the only lawful means: marriage for free women and ownership for slave-girls. This is the foundation of Islamic family law.
3
Examine the proofs
Two proofs are given: first, the Quranic verse commanding flogging for adultery; second, the historical case of Ma'iz who was stoned by the Prophet's order. Both show that such acts are punishable, hence unlawful.
If it were lawful, Ma'iz would not have been punished.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من قال : إذا بلغ العبد في الحب غاية المحبة تحل له نساء الغير وإماء الغير، فهن كالرياحين له أن يشمهن لأن هذا حبيب الله والنساء إماء الله، والحبيب لا يمنع حبيبه عما يريد. وقال المسلمون وهم أهل السنة والجماعة : لا تحل النساء إلا بالنكاح، والإماء إلا بالملك وبالنكاح أيضًا إذا زوجها المولى من غيره تحل له وهى أمته يدل عليه قال الله تعالى: ﴿الزانية والزاني فاجلدوا كل واحد منهما مائة جلدة﴾ [النور: ٢] ولأن ماعزا زنى فرجم، فلو كان حلالا لما استحق الرجم.
And among them are those who said: When the slave reaches the utmost degree of love, the women of others and the slave-girls of others become lawful for him, for they are like flowers for him to smell, because he is the beloved of Allah and women are the slave-girls of Allah, and the beloved is not prevented by his beloved from what he desires. And the Muslims, who are Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama‘ah, said: Women are not lawful except through marriage, and slave-girls are not lawful except through ownership, and also through marriage when the master marries her to someone else she becomes lawful for him while she is his slave-girl. This is indicated by Allah Almighty saying: {The adulteress and the adulterer: flog each one of them one hundred lashes} [al-Nur 24:2] and because Ma'iz committed adultery and was stoned. If it were lawful, he would not have deserved stoning.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer. First, Imam al-Nasafi reports the claim of a deviant group: they assert that when a person reaches the highest level of love (for God or for a saint?), others' women and slave-girls become lawful for him, comparing them to flowers that he may smell. Their justification is that such a person is a 'beloved of Allah' and women are 'slave-girls of Allah', so the beloved is not denied anything by his beloved. This is a dangerously antinomian view. The response from Ahl al-Sunnah is clear and decisive. They assert the only lawful means of sexual relations: marriage for free women and ownership (or marriage by the master) for slave-girls. They provide two pieces of evidence. First, the Quranic verse (al-Nur 24:2) that prescribes flogging for fornication, implying that such acts are forbidden and punishable. Second, the case of Ma'iz ibn Malik who committed adultery and was stoned by the Prophet's order. If such acts were lawful for the 'beloved', he would not have been punished. Thus, the claim is refuted by both textual proof and logical implication from punishment.

Key Terms
حلّ النساء
نكاح
ملك
زنا
رجم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Extreme love for Allah or His saints permits sexual relations with any woman, regardless of marriage.
Correction: Islamic law clearly limits lawful sexual relations to marriage or ownership; even the Prophet's companions and saints were subject to the Shari'ah.

Checkpoint
What evidence does Imam al-Nasafi use to refute the claim that extreme love makes others' women lawful?
A) The consensus of scholars alone
B) The Quranic punishment for adultery and the stoning of Ma'iz
C) The saying that love is blind
D) The argument that flowers are not to be eaten

Key Takeaway
The Shari'ah is not suspended for the 'beloved of Allah'; lawful relations require marriage or ownership.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there any desire you have justified by telling yourself that your sincerity or devotion to Allah exempts you from His clear command? How will you surrender that rationalization today?
?
If you truly believed that your 'love of Allah' could override His law, what would that say about your view of His authority? Are you willing to submit even when His rulings contradict your wants?
?
The deviant group reduced women to objects for their pleasure, calling them 'flowers'. Where in your own heart do you treat people as means to satisfy your desires instead of honoring the boundaries Allah set? What concrete step will you take to repent and respect those boundaries?

Divine Love Does Not Abolish Obligations
Nasafi refutes antinomianism using prophetic examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Ahl al-Sunna, divine love intensifies rather than removes religious obligations, as demonstrated by the prophets.

Core Idea
The closer to Allah, the heavier the obligation.

Some claim that when a person reaches the pinnacle of love for God, religious commands fall away. This passage shows the orthodox Sunni response: the opposite is true. The most beloved of Allah, the prophets, bore the heaviest duties and were held most accountable. By examining their examples, we see that love and obligation go hand in hand.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the heretical view and the Sunni refutation.
Pay attention to the key terms like 'amr wa nahy' and 'takleef'.
2
Identify the two positions
The passage presents a heretical claim and the Ahl al-Sunna response. Note the different conclusions about the relationship between love and obligation.
3
Examine the prophetic examples
Study how Prophet Muhammad, Adam, and David are cited to prove that even the most beloved are commanded and rebuked.
The examples show both commands and consequences of disobedience.
4
Reflect on the hadiths
The passage ends with hadiths about hardship faced by prophets and their families, reinforcing that obligation and difficulty accompany high rank.
Consider the lesson: love does not mean exemption from trial.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من قال : إذا بلغ العبد في الحبّ غاية المحبة سقط عنه الأمر والنهي ويحل له ما اشتهى، وحبيب الله تعالى لو خُيّر بين الكفر والقتل يختار قتل نفسه، فهو حبيب غاية المحبة، وكل من لم يكن منافقا فهو حبيب الله. وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: العبد لا يسقط عنه الأمر والنهي، وكلّ من كان أقرد إلى الله تعالى يُكلَّف بأشد التكليف كالنبي الله كان حبيبه وصفيه وقام إلى الصلاة حتى تورمت قدماه وقد أمره بأوامر منها قوله تعالى: ﴿يَتَأَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ اتَّقِ اللَّهَ ﴾ [الأحزاب: ١] وقوله تعالى: ﴿قُ الَّيْلَ إِلَّا قَلِيلا نِصْفَهُ أَو أَنقُصْ مِنْهُ قَلِيلًا ﴾ [المزمل: ٢-٣] وقوله تعالى: ﴿يَاتها الرُّسُلُ كُلُوا مِنَ الطَّيِّبَتِ وَاعْمَلُواْ صَلِحًا ﴾ [[المؤمنون: ٥١]] . وكذلك آدم عليه السلام كان حبيبه وصفيه ونهاه عن أكل الشجرة بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا نَقَرَبَا هَذِهِ الشَّجَرَةَ ﴾ [البقرة: ٣٥] فلما أكل منها عاتبه وأخرجه من الجنة. وكذلك داود عليه السلام لما نظر إلى امرأة أوريا عاتبه الله بذلك، ورُوِيَ عن عائشة رضِيَ الله عنها قالت: «ما شبع آل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ثلاثة أيام متواليات من خبز بر مرتين حتى قُبِضَ». كذلك روى عن النبي أنه قال: «مات سبعون نبياً في يوم واحد من الجوع والقمل».
And among them is one who said: When the servant reaches the utmost degree of love, command and prohibition fall away from him, and what he desires becomes lawful for him. And the beloved of Allah Almighty, if he were given the choice between disbelief and death, would choose to kill himself, so he is a beloved of utmost love, and everyone who is not a hypocrite is a beloved of Allah. And the Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a said: Command and prohibition do not fall away from the servant, and everyone who is closer to Allah Almighty is charged with the most severe obligation, like the Prophet of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, for he was His beloved and chosen, and he stood for prayer until his feet swelled, and He commanded him with commands, including His saying: {O Prophet, fear Allah} [Al-Ahzab: 1] and His saying: {Stand the night except a little, half of it or reduce from it a little} [Al-Muzzammil: 2-3] and His saying: {O messengers, eat from the good things and do righteous deeds} [Al-Mu'minun: 51]. And likewise Adam, peace be upon him, was His beloved and chosen, and He forbade him from eating the tree by His saying: {And do not approach this tree} [Al-Baqara: 35]; when he ate from it, He rebuked him and brought him out of Paradise. And likewise David, peace be upon him, when he looked at the wife of Uriah, Allah rebuked him for that. And it is narrated from Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, she said: 'The family of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, never ate their fill of barley bread for three consecutive nights until he died.' Likewise it is narrated from the Prophet that he said: 'Seventy prophets died in one day from hunger and lice.'
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage contrasts a heretical view with the orthodox position of Ahl al-Sunna. The heretical claim is that extreme love grants exemption from divine commands and prohibitions, and that the beloved would prefer death over disbelief, implying that all non-hypocrites are beloveds. The Ahl al-Sunna response firmly rejects this: commands and prohibitions never fall away from any servant. In fact, those closer to Allah bear heavier obligations. Proof is given by citing the Prophet Muhammad, who despite being the beloved, was commanded with intense worship and prohibitions (e.g., fear Allah, stand in night prayer). Examples of Adam and David show that even prophets were commanded and rebuked for sins. Finally, a hadith about the Prophet's family and another about prophets suffering hunger and lice illustrate that hardship and obligation remain even for the most beloved.

Key Terms
الأمر والنهي
المحب
التكليف
أهل السنة والجماعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Extreme love for God exempts a person from observing commands and prohibitions.
Correction: According to Ahl al-Sunna, the closer one is to Allah, the heavier the obligations, as shown by the prophets.

Checkpoint
What is the Ahl al-Sunna position regarding the relationship between divine love and religious obligations?
A) Extreme love removes all obligations.
B) The closer one is to God, the lighter the obligations.
C) Commands and prohibitions never fall away; the beloved bear heavier obligations.
D) Only prophets are exempt from some obligations.

Key Takeaway
Love for Allah does not exempt from obligations; rather, the greater the love, the greater the responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you felt that following Allah's commands is too burdensome or restrictive? How does this lesson challenge that feeling and call you to reconsider your attitude toward obligations?
?
Which are you more like: the antinomian who desires an easy path with no duties, or the prophets who bore heavy responsibilities despite being Allah's beloved? What would change in your daily life if you truly believed that closeness to Allah means more responsibility, not less?
?
Think of one specific command of Allah that you have been neglecting or rationalizing away. Based on this lesson, what concrete step will you take today to fulfill that obligation, regardless of your feelings about it?
